Testimony of Sons on Father's Will: Istihsan Overrides Qiyas
Ruling on sons' testimony about father's will with executor's acceptance or denial

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on testimony of sons regarding their father's will, distinguishing the two scenarios based on the executor's acceptance, and apply the principle of istihsan versus qiyas.

Core Idea
Sons' testimony accepted by istihsan when executor agrees; rejected when he denies.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq examines a specific case: two sons testify that their father appointed a certain person as executor. The ruling surprises by accepting this testimony despite the sons' apparent benefit. The key lies in istihsan (juridical preference) over strict qiyas. Understanding this distinction reveals how Hanafi fiqh balances textual consistency with practical justice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling and Two Scenarios
Read the passage to discern the basic ruling: when the executor accepts the will, the sons' testimony is accepted; when he denies, it is rejected. Note the conditional nature.
The passage emphasizes that 'claim' here means consent, not litigation.
2
Understand the Qiyas Objection
Recognize the hypothetical ruling by qiyas: the testimony should be rejected because the sons have a personal interest (the executor might benefit them). This is the default legal analogy.
Qiyas is the baseline; istihsan overrides it.
3
Grasp the Istihsan Rationale
Analyze the hanafi response: the judge already has the authority to appoint an executor independently. The testimony merely spares him the burden of identification; it does not establish a new right. Therefore, the benefit to the witnesses is irrelevant.
Istihsan is applied because the testimony is facilitative, not constitutive.
4
Apply the Distinction: Real Testimony vs. Informational Statement
Contrast this with a case where death is not known: then the judge cannot appoint an executor without the testimony, so it becomes a real testimony and the benefit disqualifies it. Here, since death is known, the testimony is merely informational, like a lottery (qur'a).
The key is whether the testimony is essential for the judge to act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو شهدا أي لو مات رجل وترك ابنين فشهدا أن أباهما أوصى إليه، والوصي يدعي جاز، وإن أنكر لا. المراد من الدعوى هنا الرضاء؛ إذ الجواز لا يتوقف على الدعوى، بل للقاضي أن ينصب وصياً إذا رضي به جاز أي شهادة الابنين، وهذا الجواز استحسان، والقياس أن لا تقبل؛ لأن الشاهد لنفسه نفعاً، وجه الاستحسان: أن للقاضي ولاية نصب الوصي، وهذه الشهادة كفته مؤونة التعيين، لا أنه ثبت بها شيء لم يكن للقاضي فعله، بخلاف ما إذا لم يكن الموت ظاهراً؛ لأنه حينئذ لا يملك القاضي نصب الوصي إلا بهذه البينة وفيها تهمة لجر النفع إلى الشاهد. وإن أنكر لا أي إن أنكر الرجل الوصية لا تقبل شهادتهما؛ لأن القاضي لا يجبر أحداً على قبول الوصية، والحاصل أن شهادة الابنين في صورة رضاء الوصي يجوز؛ لأنها ليست بشهادة حقيقة؛ إذ الشهادة الحقيقية توجب على القاضي ما لا يتمكن منه بدونها، وهذه ليست كذلك؛ لتمكنه من نصب الوصي إذا رضي الوصي، والموت معروف؛ حفظاً لأموال الناس، لكن عليه أن يتأمل في صلاحية من ينصبه، وبهذه الشهادة كفى مؤونة التعيين، ولم يثبت الشهود بها شيئاً آخر، فصارت كالقرعة في كونها ليست بحجة، بل هي واقعة لمؤونته تعيين القاضي.
And if two (sons) testify: meaning, if a man dies leaving two sons, and they testify that their father had made a will to a certain person (executor), and the executor claims (i.e., accepts), it is permissible; and if he denies, not. What is meant by 'claim' here is consent; for permissibility does not depend on claim, rather the judge has authority to appoint an executor if the person consents. 'Permissible' means the testimony of the two sons is permissible, and this permissibility is istihsan; qiyas would require that it not be accepted because the witness derives benefit for himself. The basis of istihsan: the judge has the authority to appoint an executor, and this testimony spares him the burden of identification; it does not establish anything the judge could not do on his own. Unlike when death is not known; then the judge cannot appoint an executor except through this evidence, and there is suspicion of drawing benefit to the witness. And if he denies: i.e., if the man denies the will, their testimony is not accepted because the judge cannot compel anyone to accept executorship. The conclusion: the testimony of the two sons when the executor consents is permissible because it is not a real testimony; real testimony obligates the judge to do something he cannot do without it, but here he can appoint an executor if the executor consents, and the death is known. This is to protect people's property. However, the judge must examine the suitability of whomever he appoints. With this testimony, the burden of identification is spared, and the witnesses do not establish anything else, so it becomes like a lottery in that it is not a proof, but a matter incidental to the judge's appointment.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage deals with the testimony of two sons that their father appointed a certain person as executor (wasi). The ruling distinguishes between two scenarios: if the nominated executor accepts the role, the sons' testimony is accepted (jaza), but if he denies, it is not. The acceptance is based on istihsan (juridical preference), not qiyas. By qiyas, the testimony would be rejected because the sons have a personal interest (the executor might benefit them). But istihsan permits it because the judge already has the power to appoint an executor; the testimony merely helps identify a willing and suitable person, sparing the judge the effort of searching. The sons do not establish any new right; they only facilitate the judge's choice. In contrast, if the executor denies, the judge cannot force him, so the testimony is useless. The author emphasizes that this is not a true testimony (shahada haqiqiyya) that binds the judge, but rather an informational statement akin to a lottery (qur'a) in its effect—it helps the judge make a decision without being a binding proof.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juridical preference that overrides qiyas; here, accepting testimony despite apparent benefit to witnesses because the judge already has authority to appoint.
شهادة حقيقية (shahada haqiqiyya): A real testimony that obligates the judge to rule based on it; here contrasted with the sons' statement which is merely informational.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the testimony of two sons about their father's will accepted by istihsan despite qiyas suggesting rejection?
A) Because the sons are inherently trustworthy.
B) Because the judge already has authority to appoint an executor, so the testimony only helps identify a willing person.
C) Because the father's will confirms the testimony.
D) Because the sons have no personal interest.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts sons' testimony on their father's will by istihsan when the executor accepts, because the judge already has the authority to appoint an executor.

Testimony of Sons on Father's Agency Rejected
Ruling that sons' testimony on father's agency is rejected due to tuhma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sons' testimony about their father's agency and explain why it is rejected due to tuhma.

Core Idea
Sons' testimony about their father's agency is always rejected because they benefit from it.

In this passage, we continue the discussion of testimony (shahada) and its disqualifiers. The specific case is when two sons testify that their absent father appointed someone as an agent (wakil) to collect debts. The ruling is clear: such testimony is not accepted, whether the agent confirms or denies it. The reason is tuhma (suspicion) that the sons are testifying for their father's benefit, which is a disqualifier in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Read the passage and note the specific case: two sons testify that their absent father appointed an agent to collect debts. The ruling is that this testimony is not accepted.
2
Understand the reason (tuhma)
The text explicitly gives the reason: tuhma (suspicion) because the sons are testifying for their father, which benefits them. In Hanafi law, any suspicion of partiality disqualifies testimony.
Tuhma is a strict disqualifier; actual bias need not be proven.
3
Compare with the previous ruling on wills
The commentary notes a contrast: in the case of a will (discussed earlier), the judge could independently appoint an executor. Here, the judge cannot appoint an agent for an absent person (except for a missing person), so the testimony is the sole basis, which is tainted.
4
Recognize the generality of the rule
The term 'two sons' is explained to mean anyone whose testimony is not accepted for the principal. That is, any relative who would benefit from the testimony is disqualified.
This includes other close relatives, not just sons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كما لو شهدا أن أباهما الغائب وكل فلاناً بقبض ديونه، وهذا القيد اتفاقي، إذ لو شهدا أن أباهما وكله بالخصومة لم تقبل أيضاً، والمراد بالابنين كل من لا تقبل شهادته للموكل، وإنما لا تقبل هذه الشهادة، سواء ادعى الوكيل أو أنكر لتهمته؛ لأن القاضي لا يملك نصب الوكيل عن الغائب إلا في المفقود، فلو ثبتت الوكالة لثبت شهادتهما، وهي غير موجبة لأجل التهمة؛ لأنهما يشهدان لأبيهما، فبطلت.
As if they testify that their absent father appointed someone to collect his debts—this restriction is agreed upon, for if they testify that their father appointed him for litigation, it would also not be accepted. By 'two sons' is meant anyone whose testimony for the principal is not accepted. This testimony is not accepted, whether the agent claims or denies, due to the suspicion (tuhma) because the judge cannot appoint an agent for an absent person except in the case of a missing person. If the agency were established, their testimony would be established, but it is not effective due to suspicion, because they testify for their father, so it is invalid.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage provides an analogy to the previous ruling. If two sons testify that their absent father appointed someone as his agent (wakil) to collect debts, their testimony is not accepted at all—whether the agent accepts or denies. The reason is tuhma (suspicion of partiality): the sons are testifying in favor of their father, which is a clear benefit to them. Furthermore, the judge generally lacks authority to appoint an agent for an absent person (except in cases of a missing person, mafqud). Therefore, unlike the will case where the judge could independently appoint, here the testimony would be the sole basis for establishing agency, and since it is tainted, it is rejected. The ruling extends to any testimony where the witnesses are related to the principal.

Key Terms
تهمة (tuhma): Suspicion of partiality or bias that renders testimony inadmissible; here because the sons testify for their father's benefit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the testimony of two sons about their father's agency rejected even if the agent confirms it?
A) Because the sons are minors.
B) Because of tuhma (suspicion) that they are benefiting their father.
C) Because the father is absent and cannot be cross-examined.
D) Because agency cannot be established by testimony alone.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, testimony from a close relative about an absent principal's agency is always rejected due to tuhma, regardless of the agent's response.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

The Judge and Testimony on Mere Jarh
Ruling that testimony on mere jarh is not heard unless it involves a legal right.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when testimony for jarh is admissible, distinguish it from the Shafi'i position, and apply the exceptions involving legal rights.

Core Idea
Jarh is heard only when it establishes a legal right, not to merely expose sin.

This lesson examines a key procedural rule in Hanafi fiqh: a judge does not accept testimony that solely seeks to disparage witnesses (jarh). The rationale is the command to cover Muslims' faults. However, if the jarh is tied to establishing a right of God or a personal right, or to repelling public harm, it becomes admissible. We will also contrast the Hanafi view with the Shafi'i position, which accepts such testimony directly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the opening statement: 'The judge does not hear testimony on jarh.' Note that it specifies 'mere jarh' without a right. Understand that the judge does not rule on tafsiq alone.
The term 'jarh' here means disparagement, not necessarily proof of witness unfitness.
2
Understand the rationale: satr (covering)
The judge is commanded to cover Muslims. Exposing faults without necessity is haram. This is the Hanafi proof from the hadith about covering.
This principle overrides the desire to disqualify witnesses for general sinfulness.
3
Recognize the Shafi'i opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that such testimony is heard and the judge rules on tafsiq directly. The text states 'Upon al-Shafi'i: he hears and rules.'
The thamarah al-khilaf: in practice, Hanafi judges reject bare attacks, Shafi'i judges accept them.
4
Note the exceptions: when jarh is coupled with a right
If the jarh involves a right of God (like hadd) or a personal right (like compensation), it is accepted. The text lists examples: zina, theft, settlement, hiring, and self-defense against public harm.
The jarh becomes incidental; the main goal is preserving rights.
5
Apply to given scenarios
The text distinguishes: claims that involve a preceding right (e.g., paid to not testify) are valid; claims of hiring without payment are mere jarh and rejected. Also, confessions and public harm cases are accepted.
Pay attention to whether the claim includes a demand for return of money or other enforceable rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يسمع القاضي الشهادة على جرح. على جرح مجرد من غير أن يتضمن إيجاب حق من حقوق الشرع أو من حقوق العباد، وقيل: المراد أنه لا يسمع بعد التعديل، ولو قبله قبلت والمعنى أن القاضي لا يحكم بالشهادة على تفسيق الشهود من غير أن يتضمن إيجاب حق؛ لأن الفسق المجرد مما لا يدخل تحت الحكم، وفي "الغاية": مثال الجرح المجرد الذي لا يدخل تحت حكم القاضي كما إذا قال المدعى عليه: إن شهود المدعي فسقة، أو قال: استأجرت الشهود، وعند الشافعي: يسمع ويحكم به. ولنا: أن القاضي مأمور بالستر على المسلمين، وفي سماع البينة هتك الحرمة وإشاعة الفاحشة، وذلك حرام إلا إذا تضمن حق الشرع والعبد فحينئذ تقبل، كما إذا قال: زنوا أو شربوا الخمر أو سرقوا أو أخذوا المال أو قتلوا فتقبل شهادتهما ضرورة إحياء الحقوق وإن كان فيه هتك الحرمة؛ لأن المقصود هو إيجاب حق الحد، أو إيجاب حق العبد وهو ضمان يدخل تحت الحكم وفي ضمنه ثبت الجرح، وكذا إذا قال المدعى عليه: إني صالحت الشهود بكذا من المال على أن لا يشهدوا عليّ بهذا الباطل، وقد شهدوا عليّ به، وأقام على ذلك بينة وطلب استرداد المال، تقبل. وكذا إذا قال: أعطاهم المدعي من مال الذي كان في يده حتى يشهدوا له بالزور وطلب استرداده بالبينة تقبل؛ لأن دعواه صحيحة؛ لما فيه من إيجاب رد المال على المشهود عليه وهو مما يدخل تحت الحكم، حتى لو قال: "صالحتهم بكذا من المال على أن يشهدوا علي، ولم أدفع لهم المال"، أو قال: "استأجر المدعي الشهود بكذا المال على أن يشهدوا له" لا تقبل؛ لأن الدعوى غير صحيحة؛ إذ المدعى به مجرد جرح؛ لأنه لم يدع قبله حقاً يمكن القضاء به، ودعوى الاستئجار وإن كانت صحيحة لكنه يدعيها لغيره، وليس له ولاية الإلزام لغيره، فكان جرحاً مجرداً، ولو أقام البينة على إقرار المدعي أن الشهود فسقة، تقبل بينته. وكذا إذا أقامها على إقراره أنه استأجرهم، أو على إقرارهم أنهم لم يحضروا المجلس الذي كان فيه الحق، وكذا إذا أقامها على إقراره أنهم عبيد أو محدودون في قذف فحينئذ تقبل؛ لما فيها من إثبات حق الله تعالى أو العبد، والحاجة ماسة إلى إحيائه، واعلم أن الجرح المجرد إذا تضمن دفع ضرر عام تسمع عليه البينة كرجل يؤذي المسلمين بيده ولسانه تقبل البينة عليه؛ ليمنعه القاضي عن ذلك، وهذا هو محمل لقوله عليها: "اذكر الفاسق بما فيه". جرح بالفتح أي فسق مجرد من أن يتضمن إيجاب حق الشرع والعبد، نحو أن يشهدوا أن الشهود فسقة أو زناة ونحو ذلك.
And the judge does not hear testimony on jarh (disparagement). On mere jarh without involving the establishment of a right of Shari'ah or a right of the people. And it is said: what is meant is that he does not hear it after ta'dil (declaration of uprightness); but if before, it is accepted. The meaning is that the judge does not rule based on testimony regarding tafsiq (declaring witnesses to be sinners) without involving the establishment of a right, because mere fisq is not subject to a judicial ruling. In al-Ghayah: the example of mere jarh that does not fall under the judge's ruling is when the defendant says: 'The plaintiff's witnesses are fasiqun,' or 'I hired the witnesses.' According to al-Shafi'i: he hears it and rules accordingly. Our proof: the judge is commanded to cover Muslims, and hearing such evidence would violate sanctity and spread immorality, which is haram, unless it involves a right of God or man, then it is accepted. For example, if he says: 'They committed zina, drank wine, stole, took property, or killed,' their testimony is accepted out of necessity to revive rights, even if it involves violating sanctity, because the purpose is to establish the right of hadd or the right of the slave (compensation) which falls under the ruling, and the jarh is established implicitly. Likewise, if the defendant says: 'I settled with the witnesses for such money that they would not testify against me with this falsehood, and they testified against me,' and he brings evidence and seeks return of the money, it is accepted. And likewise if he says: 'The plaintiff gave them from the money that was in his hand so that they would testify falsely for him,' and he seeks its return with evidence, it is accepted because his claim is valid, involving the establishment of returning the money to the defendant, which falls under judicial ruling. But if he says: 'I settled with them for money that they would testify against me, but I did not pay them,' or 'The plaintiff hired the witnesses for money to testify for him,' it is not accepted because the claim is not valid; what is claimed is mere jarh, as he did not claim a preceding right that can be adjudicated. The claim of hiring, though valid, he claims it for another and has no authority to compel another, so it is mere jarh. If he brings evidence of the plaintiff's confession that the witnesses are fasiqun, his evidence is accepted. Likewise if he brings evidence of his confession that he hired them, or of their confession that they did not attend the session where the right occurred, or of his confession that they are slaves or have been flogged for qadhf, then it is accepted because it involves establishing a right of God or man, and there is a pressing need to revive it. Know that mere jarh, if it involves repelling general harm, evidence is heard on it. For example, a man who harms Muslims with his hand and tongue, evidence is accepted against him so that the judge may prevent him. This is the interpretation of his saying: 'Mention the fasiq for what he has.' Jarh (with fatha) means mere fisq without involving a right of God or man, such as testifying that the witnesses are fasiqun or fornicators, etc.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage establishes the principle that a judge does not accept testimony that solely aims to disparage (jarh) witnesses without involving a legal right. The reason is that the judge is commanded to conceal the faults of Muslims, and exposing them without necessity is haram. However, if the testimony is linked to establishing a right of Allah (e.g., hadd penalties for zina, drinking, theft) or a right of an individual (e.g., compensation), then the jarh is admissible because it is incidental to a valid claim. The passage then distinguishes between examples: if the defendant claims he paid witnesses to not testify, and seeks return of money, that involves a right and is accepted. But if he claims he hired them but didn't pay, or the plaintiff hired them, that is mere jarh without a right and is rejected. Exceptions are when the jarh is based on confessions (iqrar) because confession establishes a right. Additionally, if the jarh aims to stop public harm (e.g., a person harming others), it is accepted. A brief dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i is noted: he would hear all such testimony and rule on tafsiq. The Hanafi position is supported by the principle of satr (covering faults).

Key Terms
جرح (jarh): Disparagement or accusation of fisq against witnesses; mere jarh does not involve a legal right.
تفسيق (tafsiq): Declaring someone a fasiq (sinner); the act of jarh leading to tafsiq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the Hanafi judge accept testimony that disparages witnesses (jarh)?
A) Only when the witnesses are slaves.
B) When the jarh involves establishing a right of God or man.
C) Always, as long as the witnesses are known to be sinners.
D) Never, as it is always haram.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, testimony that only disparages witnesses is not heard unless it is linked to a legal right or public harm, balancing the command to cover faults with the need to uphold justice.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
12 min
Testimony Must Agree with the Claim in Ten Aspects
States the principle of testimony-claim agreement with ten aspects and examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that testimony must agree with the claim in ten specific aspects and apply it to determine whether testimony is accepted or rejected.

Core Idea
Testimony in huquq al-ibad must match the claim in type, quantity, quality, time, place, action, passion, position, ownership, and relationship — otherwise it is rejected.

In this passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq, the author lays down the fundamental rule for testimony in civil rights: it must agree with the claim. He then elaborates ten aspects in which this agreement must exist, such as type, quantity, quality, time, place, and others. Understanding these aspects is essential for any judge or student of fiqh to correctly evaluate testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the foundational principle
The passage begins by stating that testimony in the rights of people (huquq al-ibad) is not accepted without a prior claim. This is a key condition. Conversely, testimony is accepted if it agrees with the claim. Recognize that for the rights of Allah (e.g., hudud), a claim is not required.
This principle is derived from the requirement that testimony serves to confirm or corroborate the claim; without a claim, there is nothing to confirm.
2
Distinguish between testimony for more vs. less
Note the rule: testimony for more than the claimed amount is invalid, but testimony for less is valid. The rationale is that testifying to less does not contradict the claim; it merely substantiates a part of it. However, testifying to more contradicts the claim and falsifies it.
This highlights the importance of precision in testimony.
3
Understand absolute vs. restricted ownership
The passage compares absolute ownership (al-milk al-mutlaq) with ownership by a specific cause (e.g., inheritance or purchase). Absolute ownership is considered more comprehensive and includes all times and causes. Therefore, if a claim is for absolute ownership, testimony for a specific cause is acceptable (as it is less), but the reverse is not.
This distinction is critical when the claim involves ownership.
4
List and apply the ten aspects of agreement
Study the ten aspects: type, quantity, quality, time, place, action, passion, position, ownership, and relationship. For each, the passage gives an example of a mismatch that would cause rejection. You should be able to recall all ten and explain why each must match.
Memorize these ten aspects; they are the core of this chapter.
5
Apply to given examples and edge cases
Work through the examples provided: claim of 10 dinars vs. testimony of 10 dirhams (type mismatch), claim of 9 dirhams vs. testimony of 15 dirhams (quantity mismatch), etc. Then consider the edge case where the claim is for a specific cause (inheritance) and testimony is for absolute ownership — it is rejected. The reverse is accepted.
The key is to determine whether the testimony contradicts the claim or merely narrows it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاختلاف في الشهادة أي في بيان أحكامه الشهادة إن وافقت الدعوى قبلت وإلا لا . ادّعى دارا. أي لا تقبل رجل على آخر باب: لما ذكر مسائل الاتفاق وهو الأصل، شرع في مسائل ،الاختلاف ومبنى الباب على أصول: منها: أن الشهادة على حقوق العباد لا تقبل بلا دعوى بخلاف حقوقه تعالى ومنها : أن الشهادة بأكثر من المدعى باطلة، بخلاف الأقل؛ للاتفاق فيه ومنها أن الملك المطلق أزيد من المقيد؛ لثبوته من الأصل، والملك بالسبب مقتصر على وقت السبب، ومنها: موافقة الشهادتين لفظاً ، ومعنى، وموافقة الشهادة الدعوى معنى فقط. (فتح)] قد عرفت معنى الشهادة من قبل، والدعوى: هي مطالبة حق في مجلس من له ولاية الخلاص عند ثبوته والمراد بموافقتهما: أن يكون الدعوى والشهادة متحدين في عشرة أشياء: النوع والكم والكيف والزمان والمكان والفعل والانفعال والوضع والملك والنسبة، فإن خالف الشهادة في أحد هذه الأشياء، لم تكن موافقة للدعوى، مثلاً. إذا ادعى على آخر عشرة دنانير وشهد الشاهد بعشرة دراهم في النوع أو ادعى تسعة دراهم وشهد بخمسة عشر، في الكم، أو ادعى سرقة ثوب أحمر، وشهد بأبيض في الكيف، أو ادعى قتل وليه يوم النحر بالكوفة، وشهد بذلك يوم الفطر بالبصرة في الزمان والمكان أو ادعى شق زقه وإتلاف ما فيه بالشق، وشهد بانشقاقه عنده، في الفعل والانفعال، أو ادعى عقاراً بالجانب الشرقي من ملك فلان، وشهد بالغربي منه، في الوضع، أو ادعى أنه ملكه وشهد أنه ملك ابنه في الملك، أو ادعى أنه عبده ولدته الجارية ،الفلانية وشهد بولادة غيرها، في النسبة لم تكن الشهادة موافقة للدعوى في الصور كلها. وفي قوله: "إن وافقت الدعوى إشارة إلى أن تقدم الدعوى في حقوق العباد شرط قبول الشهادة، فتقبل فيما توافق الدعوى؛ لإمكان قضاء القاضي بها، وأما الموافقة بين لفظيهما فليست بشرط، ألا تری أن المدعي يقول: أدعي على غريمي هذا والشاهد يقول : أشهد بذلك. (عيني، فتح، عناية) قبلت : أي الشهادة؛ لأنها طابقت الدعوى فأمكن قضاء القاضي بها (عيني) وإلا لا : [ أي وإن لم يوافق الشهادة الدعوى بأن كانت بألف قرض وشهدا بألف ثمن متاع (عيني)] أي وإن لم يوافق الشهادة الدعوى لا تقبل؛ لأنها خالفت الدعوى، فلم يمكن القضاء بها؛ وذلك لأن الشهادة لأجل تصديق الدعوى، فإذا خالفتها فقد كذبتها، والدعوى الكاذبة لا تعتبر، فانعدم الشرط، وهو تقدم تصديق الدعوى، فلا يحكم بها ، بخلاف حقوق الله تعالى؛ لأن الدعوى ليست فيها بشرط [ رمز الحقائق: ١٥٢/٢] ادعى داراً وكذا لو ادعى ديناً بقرض فشهدا بملك مطلق. (فتح) إرثاً أو شراء، فشهدا بملك مطلق لغت، وبعكسه لا: أي إذا ادعى ملكاً مطلقاً، فشهدا بملكه بسبب معين كالشراء والإرث تقبل؛ لأنهما شهدا بأقل مما ادعی، وكون المشهود به أقل من المدعى لا يمنع قبول الشهادة؛ فإن المراد من موافقتهما مطابقتهما أو كون المشهود به أقل. (عيني، فتح)
Chapter of disagreement in testimony, i.e., in explaining its rulings. Testimony: if it agrees with the claim, it is accepted; otherwise not. For example, he claimed a house. That is, it is not accepted. Chapter: When he mentioned matters of agreement, which is the foundation, he began with matters of disagreement. The foundation of the chapter is on principles: Among them: testimony regarding the rights of people is not accepted without a claim, unlike the rights of Allah. Among them: testimony for more than what is claimed is invalid, unlike less, due to agreement on it. Among them: absolute ownership is more than restricted ownership because it is established from the origin, while ownership by cause is limited to the time of the cause. Among them: agreement of the two testimonies in wording and meaning, and agreement of testimony with claim only in meaning. (Fath) Disagreement includes the testimony opposing the claim, disagreement of the two witnesses, and disagreement of two groups. (Fath) Testimony [i.e., whether it agrees with the claim or the attested amount is less. (Fath)] You already know the meaning of testimony. The claim is: a demand for a right in a court before one who has authority to adjudicate upon its establishment. The intended meaning of their agreement is that the claim and testimony are united in ten things: type, quantity, quality, time, place, action, passion, position, ownership, and relationship. If the testimony opposes the claim in any of these things, it is not in agreement with the claim. For example, if he claims ten dinars against another and the witness testifies to ten dirhams in type, or he claims nine dirhams and the witness testifies to fifteen in quantity, or he claims theft of a red garment and the witness testifies to a white one in quality, or he claims the murder of his relative on the day of Nahr in Kufa and the witness testifies to that on the day of Fitr in Basra in time and place, or he claims the cutting of his waterskin and destruction of its contents by cutting, and the witness testifies to its splitting in his presence in action and passion, or he claims property on the eastern side of so-and-so's property and the witness testifies to the western side in position, or he claims that it is his property and the witness testifies that it is his son's property in ownership, or he claims that he is his slave born to such-and-such a slave-girl and the witness testifies to the birth of another in relationship, the testimony is not in agreement with the claim in all these cases. In His saying: "If it agrees with the claim," there is an indication that the precedence of the claim in the rights of people is a condition for the acceptance of testimony. So it is accepted in what agrees with the claim because the judge can rule by it. As for agreement between their wordings, it is not a condition. Do you not see that the plaintiff says: I claim against this debtor of mine, and the witness says: I testify to that. (Ayni, Fath, Inayah) It is accepted: i.e., the testimony, because it matched the claim so the judge could rule by it. (Ayni) Otherwise not: i.e., if the testimony does not agree with the claim, e.g., it was for a loan of a thousand and they testified to a thousand as the price of goods (Ayni), i.e., if the testimony does not agree with the claim, it is not accepted because it opposed the claim, so ruling by it is not possible. This is because testimony is to confirm the claim; if it opposes it, it has falsified it, and a false claim is not considered. So the condition is absent, which is the prior confirmation of the claim, so no ruling is given by it. Unlike the rights of Allah because the claim is not a condition therein. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/152] He claimed a house, and also if he claimed a debt by loan and they testified to absolute ownership. (Fath) Inheritance or purchase, and they testified to absolute ownership, it is void; and the opposite is not: i.e., if he claimed absolute ownership and they testified to his ownership by a specific cause like purchase or inheritance, it is accepted because they testified to less than what he claimed. And the fact that the attested amount is less than the claim does not prevent acceptance of testimony, because the intended meaning of their agreement is either exact correspondence or that the attested amount is less. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (though the proof is implicit in the principles). It opens the chapter on disagreement in testimony. The base text states: 'Testimony: if it agrees with the claim, it is accepted; otherwise not.' The commentary then lists foundational principles for the entire chapter. First, testimony regarding the rights of people (huquq al-ibad) is not accepted without a prior claim, unlike the rights of Allah (huquq Allah) where a claim is not necessary. Second, testimony for more than what is claimed is invalid, but testimony for less is valid due to agreement. Third, absolute ownership (al-milk al-mutlaq) is greater than restricted ownership because it is established from the origin, while ownership by a specific cause is limited to that time. Fourth, the two testimonies must agree in wording and meaning, but the testimony need only agree with the claim in meaning, not wording. The passage then defines agreement in ten aspects: type, quantity, quality, time, place, action, passion, position, ownership, and relationship. Examples are given for each. The commentary emphasizes that the claim must precede testimony in huquq al-ibad; without a claim, testimony is not accepted. The judge can only rule if the testimony matches the claim. If the testimony contradicts the claim, it is as if it falsifies the claim, so it is rejected. An exception is made for rights of Allah. Finally, the passage discusses cases where the claim is for a specific cause (inheritance or purchase) but the witnesses testify to absolute ownership, and the reverse. Testimony for absolute ownership when a specific cause is claimed is void because it exceeds the claim, while testimony for a specific cause when absolute ownership is claimed is accepted because it is less than the claim.

Key Terms
الشهادة (al-shahada): Testimony given in court by a witness regarding a right.
الدعوى (al-da'wa): The claim made by a plaintiff in court demanding a right.
الملك المطلق (al-milk al-mutlaq): Absolute ownership, not restricted to a specific cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a plaintiff claims a loan of 1000 dirhams, and both witnesses testify that they sold him goods worth 1000 dirhams, is the testimony accepted according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Yes, because the amount matches.
B) No, because the type of claim (loan vs. sale) differs, so the testimony does not agree with the claim in type.
C) Yes, because both involve 1000 dirhams.
D) No, because there must be a prior claim.

Key Takeaway
Testimony in huquq al-ibad is accepted only if it agrees with the claim in ten specific aspects, with the exception that testifying to less than the claim is permissible.

Agreement Between Witnesses: Verbal and Substantive Concordance (Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Tadammun)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on witness agreement by inclusion (tadammun)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirement of witness agreement and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on tadammun, and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Two witnesses must agree in meaning; Abu Hanifa requires direct verbal match, but the Sahibayn accept inclusion (tadammun) for the lesser amount.

In Hanafi judicial procedure, the testimonies of two witnesses must be in agreement for a claim to be established. This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa insists on direct verbal concordance, while his two chief disciples consider agreement in meaning sufficient, even if one amount is included in the other. Understanding this nuanced ikhtilaf is crucial for judges and muftis assessing conflicting testimonies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Agreed Rule
All Hanafi imams agree that witnesses must agree in meaning; difference in wording due to synonymy (taraduf) does not prevent acceptance.
Example: 'hibah' and 'atiyyah' are synonymous.
2
Locate the Dispute
The dispute arises when one testimony is included in the other by tadammun, e.g., one witnesses 40 dirhams, the other 50 dirhams.
The key question: does this count as agreement?
3
State Abu Hanifa's View
Abu Hanifa requires direct verbal concordance (wad'); if the wordings differ, they are like contradictory testimonies and both are rejected.
He argues that 'one wording does not express the other, neither literally nor figuratively.'
4
State the Sahibayn's View
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad accept tadammun: the lesser is contained in the greater, so there is agreement on the lesser. Judgment is given for the lesser amount, and the plaintiff must swear for the remainder.
They focus on agreement in meaning only.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
Later Hanafi fatwa adopts the Sahibayn's view for ease (taysir), making it the operative position.
Thus, if one says 40 and the other 50, the judge awards 40 dirhams with plaintiff oath for the extra 60.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويعتبر اتفاق الشاهدين لفظا ومعنى أي الموافقة بين شهادة الشاهدين شرط قبولها كما كانت شرطاً بين الدعوى والشهادة ولكنهم اختلفوا في أنها شرط من حيث اللفظ والمعنى، أو من حيث المعنى خاصة، فأما الموافقة من حيث المعنى، فلابد منها بلا خلاف واختلاف اللفظ من حيث الترادف لا يمنع بلا خلاف، ولهذا إذا شهد أحدهما بالهبة والآخر بالعطية فهي مقبولة وأما اختلاف اللفظ بحيث يدل بعضه على مدلول بعض الآخر بالتضمن، فقد نفاه أبو حنيفة، وقال المعتبر تطابق اللفظين على إفادة المعنى بطريق الوضع لا بطريق التضمن، وعندهما: الاتفاق بالتضمن جائز، حتى لو ادعى مائة درهم فشهد شاهد بأربعين وآخر بخمسين، لا تقبل عند أبي حنيفة؛ لعدم التطابق بينهما بطريق الوضع، وعندهما يقضى بأربعين؛ لأن الأربعين موجودة في الخمسين والعبرة عندهما الاتفاق في المعنى لا غير. وكذا إن شهد أحدهما بألف وآخر بألفين لا تقبل عنده؛ لعدم المطابقة، وعندهما تقبل على الألف إذا كان المدعي يدعي ألفين وعلى هذا الخلاف المائة والمائتان والطلقة والطلقتان أو الثلاث، وبقولهما قالت الثلاثة، ولكن عندهما يحلف المدعي، ويستحق الزيادة لهما أنهما اتفقا على الأقل، فيثبت لوجود الحجة، وتفرد أحدهما بالزيادة، فلا تثبت لعدم الحجة، وله أن اختلاف اللفظ يدل على اختلاف المعنى؛ لأن لفظ الواحد غير لفظ الاثنين، ولفظ الألف غير لفظ الألفين و لم يشهد على كل واحد منهما إلا واحد فلم يثبت واحد من اللفظين؛ لأن أحد اللفظين لا يعبر به عن الآخر، لا حقيقة ولا مجازاً ، فكان كلام كل منهما كلاماً مبايناً لكلام الآخر، وصار اختلافهما هذا كاختلافهما في جنس المال بأن شهد أحدهما بكر شعير، والآخر بكر حنطة. (عيني، فتح، عناية)
And the agreement of the two witnesses is considered in wording and meaning, i.e., the concordance between the testimony of the two witnesses is a condition for its acceptance, just as it was a condition between the claim and the testimony. But they differed regarding whether it is a condition in terms of wording and meaning, or meaning alone. As for agreement in meaning, it is indispensable without disagreement. And difference in wording due to synonymy does not prevent [acceptance] without disagreement. Hence if one witness testifies to hibah (gift) and the other to atiyyah (gift), it is accepted. As for difference in wording such that one indicates the meaning of the other by inclusion (tadammun), Abu Hanifa denied it. He said the consideration is the concordance of the two wordings in conveying the meaning by direct indication (wad'), not by inclusion. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), agreement by inclusion is permissible. Thus, if he claims one hundred dirhams, and one witness testifies to forty and another to fifty, it is not accepted according to Abu Hanifa due to lack of direct concordance. According to them, judgment is given for forty because forty is contained in fifty. According to them, the criterion is agreement in meaning only. Likewise, if one testifies to a thousand and another to two thousand, it is not accepted according to him due to lack of direct correspondence. According to them, it is accepted for one thousand if the plaintiff claims two thousand. On this difference is the hundred and two hundred, the single divorce and two divorces or three. And by their saying the three said, but according to them the plaintiff must take an oath and is entitled to the increase. Because they agreed on the lesser, so it is established due to the presence of proof, and one of them alone testified to the increase, so it is not established due to lack of proof. And according to him (Abu Hanifa), difference in wording indicates difference in meaning because the word for one is not the word for two, and the word for a thousand is not the word for two thousand, and only one witness testified to each [amount], so neither of the two wordings is established because one wording does not express the other, neither literally nor figuratively. Thus the statement of each is contradictory to the statement of the other, and this difference becomes like their difference in the type of property, e.g., one testifies to a measure of barley and the other to a measure of wheat. (Ayni, Fath, Inayah)
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. It addresses the requirement that the testimonies of two witnesses must agree. The baseline rule is that the two witnesses must agree in meaning, and difference in wording due to synonymy does not harm. The dispute arises when one witness's statement is included in the other's by tadammun (inclusion). Abu Hanifa requires direct verbal concordance (wad'), meaning the wordings must be the same or synonymous. If one witness says forty and the other fifty, they do not directly correspond; forty is contained within fifty but the wording differs. Thus, he rejects it. His disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), accept it because the two testimonies agree on the lesser amount (forty) by inclusion; the objective is agreement in meaning, not exact wording. Therefore, they rule that if a plaintiff claims one hundred dirhams, and one witness testifies to forty and the other to fifty, judgment is given for forty dirhams (the common amount). The plaintiff must swear an oath regarding the remainder? Actually, the text says the plaintiff must take an oath and is entitled to the increase? Wait: The text says 'و لكن عندهما يحلف المدعي، ويستحق الزيادة' meaning according to them (the Sahibayn) the plaintiff takes an oath and deserves the increase (the full claimed amount? Actually, it says he is entitled to the increase because they agreed on the lesser? Let's read carefully: 'ولكن عندهما يحلف المدعي، ويستحق الزيادة لهما أنهما اتفقا على الأقل، فيثبت لوجود الحجة، وتفرد أحدهما بالزيادة، فلا تثبت لعدم الحجة' This means according to them, the plaintiff takes an oath and is entitled to the increase (the additional amount above what the witnesses agreed on) because they agreed on the lesser (the forty or the thousand), so that lesser is established by the testimony, and one witness alone testified to the increase (the extra ten or extra thousand), which is not established without a second witness, so the plaintiff must swear to the remainder to get it. So the plaintiff gets the lesser by testimony and the increase by oath. Abu Hanifa's view: since the wordings differ, they are like contradictory testimonies, so nothing is established. The passage equates this difference to a difference in the type of property (e.g., one says barley, the other says wheat). Thus, the Hanafi school has two positions: the stricter view of Abu Hanifa requiring direct verbal concordance, and the more relaxed view of the Sahibayn allowing tadammun. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to later Hanafi works is often that of the Sahibayn due to ease of practice.

Key Terms
التضمن (al-tadammun): Inclusion: one statement's meaning is included in the other's, e.g., forty is included in fifty.
الوضع (al-wad'): Direct linguistic indication: the literal or established meaning of a word.
الترادف (al-taraduf): Synonymy: different words with the same meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a claim for 100 dirhams, one witness testifies to 40 dirhams, the other to 50 dirhams. According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what is the outcome?
A) Both testimonies are rejected.
B) Judgment for 40 dirhams and plaintiff swears for the remainder.
C) Judgment for 50 dirhams.
D) Judgment for 100 dirhams.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that two witnesses must agree in meaning; the relied-upon view (Sahibayn) accepts inclusion (tadammun), awarding the lesser amount and requiring the plaintiff to swear for the remainder.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
12 min
Disagreement of Witnesses in Wording and Meaning: The Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on witness agreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on witness testimony when their words differ, explain Abu Hanifa's requirement of direct reference (wad') versus the Sahibayn's acceptance of implication (tadammun), and apply the mufta bihi ruling to specific scenarios.

Core Idea
When witnesses differ in wording, agreement in meaning may suffice — but Abu Hanifa demands literal correspondence.

In testimony, the witnesses' statements must agree. But what counts as agreement? If one says '40' and the other says '50', are they in agreement? This lesson explores the intra-Hanafi debate on whether agreement requires identical wording or merely overlapping meaning, and settles on the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and the dispute
The condition for testimony is agreement of witnesses. The dispute: is literal wording required or is implied agreement enough?
The text states 'ويعتبر اتفاق الشاهدين لفظا ومعنى' — agreement in wording and meaning is the condition.
2
Examine Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa requires direct linguistic reference (wad'). Words must match in wording and meaning; implication (tadammun) is not sufficient.
His dalil: 'لفظ الواحد غير لفظ الاثنين' — the word 'one' is not the word 'two'.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani accept implication. If one word's meaning includes the other, they are considered in agreement.
Their dalil: 'الأربعون موجودة في الخمسين' — forty is contained in fifty.
4
Trace the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
For a claim of 100 dirhams, one says 40, another says 50: Abu Hanifa rejects entirely; Sahibayn accept for 40 with plaintiff's oath for the remainder.
The text confirms: 'عندهما يقضى بأربعين' — according to them, judgement is for forty.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The text states 'وبقولهما قالت الثلاثة' — the later three imams follow the Sahibayn. Thus the relied-upon position is that of Sahibayn.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa in the Hanafi school.

ويعتبر اتفاق الشاهدين إلخ لفظا ومعنى أي الموافقة بين شهادة الشاهدين شرط قبولها كما كانت شرطاً بين الدعوى والشهادة ولكنهم اختلفوا في أنها شرط من حيث اللفظ والمعنى، أو من حيث المعنى خاصة، فأما الموافقة من حيث المعنى، فلابد منها بلا خلاف واختلاف اللفظ من حيث الترادف لا يمنع بلا خلاف، ولهذا إذا شهد أحدهما بالهبة والآخر بالعطية فهي ،مقبولة وأما اختلاف اللفظ بحيث يدل بعضه على مدلول بعض الآخر بالتضمن، فقد نفاه أبو حنيفة، وقال المعتبر تطابق اللفظين على إفادة المعنى بطريق الوضع لا بطريق التضمن، وعندهما: الاتفاق بالتضمن جائز، حتى لو ادعى مائة درهم فشهد شاهد بأربعين وآخر بخمسين، لا تقبل عند أبي حنيفة؛ لعدم التطابق بينهما بطريق الوضع، وعندهما يقضى بأربعين؛ لأن الأربعين موجودة في

وكذا إن شهد أحدهما بألف وآخر بألفين لا تقبل عنده؛ لعدم المطابقة، وعندهما تقبل على الألف إذا كان المدعي يدعي ألفين وعلى هذا الخلاف المائة والمائتان والطلقة والطلقتان أو الثلاث، وبقولهما قالت الثلاثة، ولكن عندهما يحلف المدعي، ويستحق الزيادة لهما أنهما اتفقا على الأقل، فيثبت لوجود الحجة، وتفرد أحدهما بالزيادة، فلا تثبت لعدم الحجة، وله أن اختلاف اللفظ يدل على اختلاف المعنى؛ لأن لفظ الواحد غير لفظ الاثنين، ولفظ الألف غير لفظ الألفين و لم يشهد على كل واحد منهما إلا واحد فلم يثبت واحد من اللفظين؛ لأن أحد اللفظين لا يعبر به عن الآخر، لا حقيقة ولا مجازاً ، فكان كلام كل منهما كلاماً مبايناً لكلام الآخر، وصار

لفظاً ومعنى: أي من حيث اللفظ والمعنى بطريق الوضع عند أبي حنيفة. (ط، عيني) لم تقبل: أي عند الإمام مطلقا كما مر، بخلاف ما لو ادعى ألفين فشهدا بألف حيث تقبل اتفاقاً. (فتح) وإن شهد: أي شهد أحدهما وشهد الشاهد الآخر إلخ. (عيني) والمدعي يدعي إلخ أي إذا شهد أحدهما بألف وشهد الآخر بألف وخمس مائة، وكان المدعي ادعى الألف والخمس مائة، تقبل الشهادة على الألف بالاتفاق لاتفاقهما على الألف لفظاً ومعنى، وتفرد أحدهما بزيادة خمس مائة بالعطف، والمعطوف غير المعطوف عليه فيثبت ما اتفقا عليه وكذا لو شهد أحدهما بطلقة والآخر بطلقة ونصف، والمدعي يدعي طلقة ونصفاً، تقبل على طلقة؛ لأن بينهما حرف العطف، بخلاف المسألة التي قبلها، حيث لا تقبل الشهادة فيها مطلقاً عنده لعدم العطف، فظهر الفرق، وقيد الدعوى بألف وخمس مائة؛ لأنه لو لم يدع الأكثر، فشهادة من شهد بالأكثر باطلة؛ لأنه كذبه المدعي إلا أن يوافق، فيقول: أصل حقي كان كما قال إلا أني استوفيت الزائد وأبرأته عنه، فحينئذ تقبل في الأقل، وعند الثلاثة يستحق المدعي في مسألة المتن خمس
مائة بحلفه. (عيني، فتح) على الألف: لاتفاقها على الألف وتفرد أحد بخمس مائة وهذا بالاتفاق. (عيني) تقبل بألف : [ أي شهادتهما بألف درهم، لاتفاقهما عليه. (عيني)] لأنهما اتفقا على وجوب الألف، فتقبل، وانفرد أحدهما بقضاء النصف، فلا تقبل؛ لعدم كمال النصاب، لا يقال: إن المدعي كذب شاهده بالقضاء، فينبغي أن لا تقبل كما إذا شهد بألف وخمس مائة، والمدعي يدعي ألفاً؛ لأنا نقول: لم يكذبه فيما شهد له، وإنما كذبه فيما شهد عليه، وذلك كما إذا شهد له اثنان بحق ثم شهدا عليه بحق لإنسان ،آخر فإن شهادتهما له لا تبطل، وإن كذبهما، لا يقدح، فكذا هذا، وعن أبي يوسف له أنه يقضي بخمس مائة فقط؛ لأن مضمون شهادة شاهد القضاء أن لا دين إلا خمس مائة في المعنى، وهو المعتبر عنده كما مر تبيين الحقائق: ١٩٨/٥] (فتح)

قضاه : [ أي قضى إلى الدائن المدعي خمس مائة لا يسمع؛ لانفراده. (عيني)] أي لم يسمع أن المديون قضى إلى الدائن خمس مائة؛ لعدم كمال الحجة ولابد أن يدعي الدائن الألف، وينكر الاستيفاء؛ إذ لو قال: لم يكن لي عليه إلا خمس مائة لم يقبل أصلاً؛ لتكذيبه شهوده، وإن اعترف بالقضاء، لزمه خمس مائة. (فتح) معه: أي مع الذي شهد بأنه قضاه (مسكين) :آخر أي شاهد آخر فحينئذ يسمع لتكمل النصاب. (عيني)
Book of Testimony. Chapter of Disagreement in Testimony. [S M] If [they testify] as inheritance or purchase, and they testify to absolute ownership, it is invalid; and the opposite is not [invalid]; and agreement of the two witnesses is required without mentioning the cause. That is, agreement between their testimonies. 'Inheritance or purchase' meaning inherited or purchased; and it is permissible that they are accusative of specification. The author left out two conditions in the claim of purchase: first, that he claims it from someone known – if he says 'my ownership I bought from Zaid' while Zaid is unknown, and the witnesses testify to absolute ownership, it is accepted; second, that he does not claim possession with purchase – if he claims both, and they testify to absolute [ownership], it is accepted. (Fath) 'Invalid' meaning the testimony; because they testified to more than what the plaintiff claimed; and they testified to an old ownership, while he claimed a newly acquired ownership... In absolute ownership, it is established from the origin so that the plaintiff is entitled to its increments. And it contains an indication that if someone undertakes testimony on ownership and wants to testify to absolute [ownership], it is not permissible. If the discrepancy between claim and testimony occurs and then they repeat the claim and testimony and agree, it is accepted. (Fath) And the opposite is not [invalid]: that is, if he claims absolute ownership, and they testify to his ownership due to a specific cause like purchase or inheritance, it is accepted; because they testified to less than what he claimed, and the fact that the testified-to is less than the claimed does not prevent acceptance of testimony; for the purpose of their agreement is correspondence or the testified-to being less. (Ayni, Fath) 'And agreement of the witnesses' etc. in wording and meaning: that is, agreement between the testimony of the two witnesses is a condition of its acceptance, just as it was a condition between claim and testimony. But they differed as to whether it is a condition in terms of wording and meaning, or in terms of meaning alone. As for agreement in meaning, it is necessary without dispute; and difference in wording by way of synonym does not prevent without dispute; hence if one witnesses a gift (hiba) and the other a gift (atiyya), it is accepted. As for difference in wording such that one indicates the meaning of the other by implication (tadammun), Abu Hanifa negated it, saying the criterion is correspondence of the two wordings in conveying the meaning by direct reference (wad'), not by implication. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), agreement by implication is permissible; such that if someone claims one hundred dirhams, and one witness testifies to forty and another to fifty, it is not accepted according to Abu Hanifa due to lack of correspondence by direct reference; but according to the two, judgement is given for forty because forty is included in fifty, and the criterion according to them is agreement in meaning only. Likewise if one witnesses a thousand and another two thousand, it is not accepted according to him due to lack of correspondence; according to the two it is accepted for the thousand if the plaintiff claims two thousand. And on this difference rest the cases of one hundred and two hundred, and one divorce and two or three divorces. And according to the two, the three (later imams) said; but according to the two, the plaintiff takes an oath and becomes entitled to the increase because they agreed on the minimum, so it is established due to the existence of proof, and one of them alone [testified to] the increase, so it is not established due to lack of proof. And for him (Abu Hanifa), difference in wording indicates difference in meaning; because the word 'one' is not the word 'two', and the word 'thousand' is not the word 'two thousand'; and not a single one of them testified to each [amount] except one, so neither of the two wordings is established; because one wording does not express the other, neither literally nor figuratively; thus the speech of each is distinct from the speech of the other, and this difference of theirs is like their difference in the type of property, such as one witnessing a load of barley and another a load of wheat. (Ayni, Fath, Inaya) ... 'Wording and meaning': that is, in terms of wording and meaning by direct reference according to Abu Hanifa. (T, Ayni) 'Not accepted': that is, according to the Imam absolutely as previously, contrary to if he claimed two thousand and they testified to a thousand, where it is accepted by agreement. (Fath) 'And if [one] witnesses' etc.: that is, one witnesses and the other witnesses etc. (Ayni) 'And the plaintiff claims' etc.: that is, if one witnesses a thousand and the other witnesses a thousand five hundred, and the plaintiff claimed a thousand five hundred, the testimony is accepted for the thousand by agreement due to their agreement on the thousand in wording and meaning, and one of them alone [testified to] the increase of five hundred by conjunction (atf), and the conjunct is not the same as the conjuncted, so what they agreed upon is established. Similarly if one witnesses a divorce and the other a divorce and a half, and the plaintiff claims a divorce and a half, it is accepted for one divorce because they have a conjunction particle, contrary to the previous case where the testimony is not accepted at all according to him due to lack of conjunction; thus the difference appears. And he restricted the claim to a thousand five hundred; because if he did not claim the larger, then the testimony of the one who testified to the larger is invalid because the plaintiff has belied him, unless he agrees by saying 'my original right was as he said but I have received the excess and discharged him from it'; then it is accepted for the smaller. And according to the three, the plaintiff in the text's case becomes entitled to five hundred by his oath. (Ayni, Fath) 'For the thousand': due to their agreement on the thousand and one alone [testified to] five hundred, and this is by agreement. (Ayni) 'Accepted for a thousand': that is, their testimony for a thousand dirhams, due to their agreement on it. (Ayni) Because they agreed on the obligation of a thousand, so it is accepted; and one alone [testified] to the payment of half, so it is not accepted due to incompleteness of the quorum. It cannot be said: 'The plaintiff belied his witness regarding the payment, so it should not be accepted, as when he testifies to a thousand five hundred and the plaintiff claims a thousand'; because we say: He did not belie him regarding what he testified for him, but rather belied him regarding what he testified against him. This is like if two testify for him for a right, then testify against him for a right to another person; his testimony for him is not invalidated even if he belies them; it does not harm. So also here. And from Abu Yusuf: he rules for five hundred only, because the purport of the testimony of the witness of payment is that there is no debt except five hundred, in meaning, and this is what is considered according to him, as in Tabyin al-Haqa'iq (5/198). (Fath) 'Paid him': that is, paid the creditor plaintiff five hundred; it is not heard due to his isolation. (Ayni) That is, it is not heard that the debtor paid the creditor five hundred due to incompleteness of proof. And the creditor must claim the thousand and deny receipt; for if he said 'I had only five hundred against him', it is not accepted at all due to his belying his witnesses; and if he acknowledges the payment, five hundred is binding on him. (Fath) 'With him': that is, with the one who testified that he paid him; 'another': that is, another witness; then it is heard to complete the quorum. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses the conditions for accepting testimony when witnesses differ in their statements, particularly regarding the cause of ownership and the amount. The author, Imam al-Nasafi, begins by stating the rule: if two witnesses testify to absolute ownership while the plaintiff claims ownership by inheritance or purchase, the testimony is invalid (لغت). Conversely, if the plaintiff claims absolute ownership and the witnesses testify to a specific cause (like purchase), the testimony is accepted because they testified to less than claimed. The key condition is that the witnesses must agree (اتفاق الشاهدين) in wording and meaning. The commentary then delves into the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether agreement requires literal correspondence in wording (as held by Abu Hanifa) or suffices by implication (as held by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The example given: if a plaintiff claims 100 dirhams, and one witness says 40, the other says 50, Abu Hanifa rejects the testimony entirely because the words 40 and 50 are not identical in wording, while the two disciples accept it for 40 because 40 is included in 50. Similarly for 1000 and 2000, and for one divorce vs. two. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn, as indicated by the phrase 'وبقولهما قالت الثلاثة' (the three later imams follow them). The passage also addresses cases where one witness testifies to 1000 and another to 1500 with the plaintiff claiming 1500: here testimony is accepted for 1000 by agreement, and the increase of 500 is considered a separate conjunct (عطف) which is not testified to by both. Another scenario: if one witness says the debt is 1000 and another says 1000 but 500 has been paid, the testimony is accepted for 1000 but the payment claim is not heard unless another witness supports it. Throughout, the commentary from Fath al-Qadir, al-Inaya, and others clarifies the reasoning and distinctions, emphasizing that in all cases the basic condition is agreement in meaning, with the debate centering on the mode of expression.

Key Terms
اتفاق الشاهدين (ittifāq al-shāhidayn): The agreement of two witnesses in their testimony, which is a condition for acceptance.
التضمن (al-taḍammun): Implication or inclusion, where one term's meaning includes another (e.g., fifty includes forty).
الوضع (al-waḍʿ): Direct linguistic reference, where a word is explicitly assigned to a meaning by language convention.
الترادف (al-tarāduf): Synonymity, where different words refer to the same meaning (e.g., hibah and atiyyah both mean gift).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Testimony is accepted for 40 dirhams.
B) Testimony is accepted for 50 dirhams.
C) Testimony is rejected entirely.
D) Testimony is accepted for 40 dirhams with the plaintiff's oath.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position accepts testimony for the minimum amount agreed upon by implication, even if the witnesses use different words.

Disagreement in Amount: Testimony on Agreed Sum Accepted
Ruling on accepting testimony when witnesses differ on amount

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting testimony when witnesses disagree on the amount, and explain the role of the claimant's oath for the excess.

Core Idea
When witnesses agree on part and differ on excess, testimony is accepted on the agreed portion; the excess may be proved by the claimant's oath.

The chapter on disagreement in testimony addresses a common courtroom dilemma: what if two witnesses give different figures? The passage distinguishes between complete disagreement (no common ground) and partial agreement (common amount plus one-sided excess). Understanding this ruling equips you to handle financial disputes where witness testimony varies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: (1) one witness says 1000, the other says 2000; (2) one says 1000, the other says 1500, and the claimant claims 1500. Distinguish them carefully.
The key difference is whether there is any common amount.
2
Apply the rule of complete disagreement
In the first scenario, there is zero overlap between the two testimonies. According to Imam Abu Hanifa (and as stated in the matn), the testimony is not accepted at all. This is because the subject matter is entirely disputed.
Contrast with the case where the claimant claims 2000 and both witnesses say 1000—that is accepted by agreement (the testimony is for less than the claim).
3
Apply the rule of partial agreement
In the second scenario, both witnesses agree on 1000, so that amount is established by two witnesses. The testimony is accepted on that agreed sum. The extra 500 is testified by only one witness, which is insufficient alone.
Partial agreement creates a foundation; the excess is treated separately.
4
Note the oath option for the excess
The three Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) rule that the claimant may take an oath to prove the additional 500. This supplements the single witness testimony and entitles the claimant to the full claimed amount (1500).
This is a unique Hanafi facility; some earlier scholars (e.g., Zufar) reportedly did not allow the oath.
5
Explain the legal reasoning
The principle is that when witnesses agree on part, that part is proven by two witnesses (the required count). The remaining part is supported by only one witness, but the claimant's oath can complete the proof. This prevents injustice where a claimant would lose the excess entirely.
The 'proof' here is a combination of testimony and oath (a form of complementary evidence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاختلاف في الشهادة. فإن شهد أحدهما بألف والآخر بألفين لم تقبل، ومعنى، فإن شهد أحدهما بألف والآخر بألفين لم تقبل: أي لم تقبل عند الإمام مطلقا كما مر، بخلاف ما لو ادعى ألفين فشهدا بألف حيث تقبل اتفاقاً. (فتح) وإن شهد أحدهما بألف وشهد الآخر بألف وخمس مائة والمدعي يدعي ذلك، قبلت على الألف، وعند الثلاثة يستحق المدعي في مسألة المتن خمس مائة بحلفه. (عيني، فتح) على الألف: لاتفاقها على الألف وتفرد أحد بخمس مائة وهذا بالاتفاق. (عيني)
Chapter on disagreement in testimony. If one witness testifies to a thousand and the other to two thousand, it is not accepted. Meaning: if one testifies to a thousand and the other to two thousand, it is not accepted at Imam (Abu Hanifa) absolutely as mentioned, unlike if he claimed two thousand and they testified to a thousand, in which case it is accepted by agreement. (Fath) And if one witnesses to a thousand and the other witnesses to a thousand five hundred, and the claimant claims that, it is accepted on the thousand. According to the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), in the issue of the text, the claimant is entitled to five hundred by his oath. (Ayni, Fath) On the thousand: because of their agreement on the thousand and one single witness's excess of five hundred, and this is by agreement. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings from the chapter on disagreement in testimony. The first ruling: if one witness says the debt is 1000 and the other says 2000, the testimony is entirely rejected according to Imam Abu Hanifa. This is because they disagree on the very subject of testimony; there is no common ground. However, if the claimant had claimed 2000 and the two witnesses both testified to 1000, that would be accepted by agreement because the testimony is for less than the claim, which is permissible. The second ruling: if one witness says 1000 and the other says 1500, and the claimant claims 1500, the testimony is accepted only for 1000 because both agree on that amount. The excess of 500 is supported by only one witness, which is insufficient for proof. However, according to the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad), the claimant can take an oath and thereby be entitled to the additional 500. The ruling is based on the principle that qadis should accept testimony on the agreed-upon portion and disregard the extra part that lacks the necessary evidentiary support.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahāda): Testimony given by witnesses in court, legally binding when conditions are met.
اختلاف (ikhtilāf): Disagreement between witnesses on the subject matter of their testimony.
ألف (alf): A thousand dirhams, a unit of currency in classical fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Testimony of Payment: When a Witness Adds That Part of the Debt Is Paid
Ruling on testimony that includes a claim of payment by the debtor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony where one witness adds a claim of payment, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute (Abu Yusuf vs. majority), and apply the analogical reasoning used to justify the ruling.

Core Idea
Agreement on the debt is accepted; additional claims require their own witnesses.

This passage addresses a common scenario in debt litigation: two witnesses confirm a debt of 1000 dirhams, but one adds that the debtor already paid 500. The ruling distinguishes between the agreed-upon debt (accepted) and the unsubstantiated payment claim (rejected). The text also discusses an ethical dilemma for the witness and an intra-Hanafi disagreement over how to handle the partial payment claim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling
Two witnesses testify to a 1000-dirham debt; one adds that 500 have been paid. The ruling: the testimony for the 1000 is accepted, but the payment claim is not because it comes from a single witness.
2
Understand the reasoning
The witnesses agree on the obligation of 1000, so that part is fully proven. The payment claim is an additional fact that requires two witnesses. The plaintiff's denial of the payment does not affect the acceptance of the debt testimony.
Analogy: if two witnesses testify for a person and later against him on a different matter, the earlier testimony remains valid.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf holds that the judge should only award 500 because the payment witness effectively reduces the debt. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) maintain the full 1000 is proven.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.
4
Consider the witness's duty
The text discusses whether the witness should testify until the plaintiff admits the payment. Some suggest the witness should only testify to the lower amount to avoid aiding oppression.
This ethical dimension shows the balance between strict evidence rules and justice.

Source Text

(عيني)] لأنهما اتفقا على وجوب الألف، فتقبل، وانفرد أحدهما بقضاء النصف، فلا تقبل؛ لعدم كمال النصاب، لا يقال: إن المدعي كذب شاهده بالقضاء، فينبغي أن لا تقبل كما إذا شهد بألف وخمس مائة، والمدعي يدعي ألفاً؛ لأنا نقول: لم يكذبه فيما شهد له، وإنما كذبه فيما شهد عليه، وذلك كما إذا شهد له اثنان بحق ثم شهدا عليه بحق لإنسان آخر فإن شهادتهما له لا تبطل، وإن كذبهما، لا يقدح، فكذا هذا، وعن أبي يوسف له أنه يقضي بخمس مائة فقط؛ لأن مضمون شهادة شاهد القضاء أن لا دين إلا خمس مائة في المعنى، وهو المعتبر عنده كما مر تبيين الحقائق: ١٩٨/٥] (فتح). قضاه : [ أي قضى إلى الدائن المدعي خمس مائة لا يسمع؛ لانفراده. (Fath) He should not testify: i.e., the witness who testified that he paid 500 of it, meaning it is obligatory upon him. (Ayni) The claimant admits: i.e., he initiates with a full thousand if he knows that he paid 500 of it. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage deals with a scenario where two witnesses testify to a debt of 1000 dirhams, but one of them adds that the debtor has already paid 500. The ruling is that the testimony is accepted for the 1000, but the claim of payment (qada') is not accepted because it comes from a single witness. The reason is that the witnesses agree on the existence of the debt (1000), so that part is established. The payment claim is additional and requires two witnesses. The objection that the plaintiff (creditor) would be denying his own witness's payment claim, which might invalidate his testimony, is answered by analogy: if two witnesses testify in favor of a person and then later testify against him in a different case, that does not invalidate their earlier favorable testimony. Similarly, here the plaintiff's denial of the payment does not nullify the accepted testimony on the debt. However, Abu Yusuf differs: he argues that the witness who testifies to payment is in effect testifying that only 500 is owed, so the judge should only award 500. The text then discusses the ethical duty of the witness: he should not testify until the plaintiff admits to having been paid the 500. A discussion follows whether this is obligatory or whether it might lead to injustice. Some scholars (following the two companions) suggest that the witness should only testify for the lesser amount (500) to avoid aiding oppression. The passage highlights the tension between strict evidentiary rules and the duty to prevent injustice.

Key Terms
قضاء (qāḍā): Payment by the debtor; a claim that the debt has been satisfied.
تكبير الشاهد (takdhīb al-shāhid): Claimant's denial of the witness's statement about payment, which does not invalidate the debt testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The judge awards only 500 because the payment claim reveals the true debt

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, where witnesses agree on a core fact, their testimony is accepted, and any additional unsubstantiated claim does not invalidate it.

Disagreement in Place or Time Invalidates Testimony for Physical Acts
Ruling on rejecting testimony when witnesses differ on location or time of an event

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that disagreement among witnesses on the time or place of a physical act invalidates their testimony, and distinguish it from disagreement about statements.

Core Idea
When witnesses disagree on where or when a physical act occurred, both testimonies are rejected — the act cannot happen in two places at once.

This passage examines a critical rule of testimony (shahadah): when witnesses contradict each other about the location or time of an event, does that ruin their credibility? The Hanafi school draws a sharp line between statements (aqwal) and physical acts (af'al). For contracts, disagreement on place is harmless because words can be repeated. But for acts like murder or theft, the same act cannot occur in two different places; thus, disagreement proves one side is lying, and both testimonies are thrown out.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
First scenario: two witnesses testify to a loan, but one adds that the debtor repaid. Second scenario: two witnesses say the killing occurred in Mecca, two others in Egypt on the same day.
The loan scenario is revisited to show the ruling on loan testimony is valid despite partial disagreement.
2
Isolate the ruling for each
In the loan case, testimony on the loan itself is valid, but the repayment part is not accepted. In the killing case, both testimonies are rejected entirely.
The rejection is because killing is a physical act.
3
Recognize the underlying principle
The author explains: if the subject matter (mashhud bihi) is a statement, disagreement on time/place does not invalidate because statements can be repeated. If it is an act or a statement whose validity requires an act, disagreement invalidates.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school.
4
Apply the qiyas
Use sale (statement) as the asl where disagreement is allowed, and killing (act) as the far'. The illah is repeatability. Since an act cannot be repeated in two places, testimonies contradict.
Rational proof (dalil aqli) is used.
5
Conclude the Hanafi position
For acts, disagreement on place, time, or instrument invalidates testimony. For statements, it does not.
There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Zufar holds the judge should not rule on the loan scenario at all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو شهدا بقرض ألف، وشهد أحدهما أنه قضاه، جازت الشهادة على القرض، ولو شهدا بأنه قتل زيداً يوم النحر بمكة، وآخران أنه قتله يوم النحر بمصر، ردّتا. بقرض ألف [ أي ألف درهم بأن شهدا أن فلاناً أقرض من فلان ألف درهم (عيني)] جازت الشهادة لثبوته بالشهادة التامة، ولا تقبل في قضاء الألف للمقرض؛ لعدم ثبوته بالحجة التامة، وذكر الطحاوي عن بعض أصحابنا أنه لا يقضي بها القاضي، وهو قول زفر عليه؛ لأن في زعم أحد الشاهدين أنه لا شيء له عليه من المال، ولو قضى لكان قضاء بشهادة الواحد، وهو غير جائز، ولأن المدعي كذب شاهد القضاء، وهو تفسيق له، قلنا: لم يكذبه في المشهود به الأول، وهو القرض، وإنما كذبه فيما عليه وهو القضاء، وهو غير الأول لا محالة، ومثله ليس بمانع في القبول والحاصل أن إكذاب المدعي شهوده تفسيق لهم؛ لكونه اختيارياً، وأما إكذابه المدعى عليه، فليس بتفسيق؛ لأنه لضرورة الدفع نفسه. (عيني، فتح، عناية) على القرض لتمام الحجة فيها ولا تقبل في القضاء لعدمها. (عيني) ردتا [ أي الشهادتان؛ لأن إحدى الطائفتين كاذبة بيقين وليست إحداهما أولى بالقبول من الآخر. (عيني)] لما أن اختلاف الشاهدين في المكان يمنع القبول، فإذا شهد شاهدان أنه قتل بمكة، وآخران بقتله بمصر قبل أن يقضي القاضي بالشهادة الأولى، لا يقبلهما؛ إذ القتل لا يمكن أن يكون في مكانين، وكذا لو اختلفا في الزمان أو الآلة التي وقع بها القتل، ولم يذكر المؤلف اختلاف الشاهدين في الزمان أو المكان، والأصل في ذلك: أن المشهود به إن كان قولا كالبيع ونحوه، فاختلاف الشاهدين لا يمنع قبول الشهادة؛ لأن القول مما يعاد، ويكرر في الأزمنة والأمكنة، وإن كان فعلاً كالغصب والقتل ونحوهما أو قولاً، لكن الفعل شرط صحته كالنكاح، فإنه قول، وحضور الشاهدين فعل، وهو شرط فاختلافهما يمنع القبول؛ لأن الفعل في زمان أو مكان غير الفعل في زمان أو مكان آخر، فاختلف المشهود به، وقد جمع العلامة المقدسي ما يكون اختلاف الشاهدين فيه في الزمان والمكان مانعاً من القبول في قوله:
And if both testify to a loan of a thousand, and one of them testifies that he (the debtor) paid it, the testimony on the loan is valid. If two testify that he killed Zayd on the day of sacrifice in Mecca, and two others that he killed him on the day of sacrifice in Egypt, both testimonies are rejected. To a loan of a thousand: [i.e., a thousand dirhams, meaning they testified that so-and-so lent so-and-so a thousand dirhams. (Ayni)] The testimony is valid due to its establishment by complete testimony, but it is not accepted for the payment of the thousand to the lender due to lack of complete proof. Al-Tahawi reported from some of our companions that the judge should not give judgment on it; that is the view of Zufar, because in the opinion of one of the two witnesses, nothing is owed, so if he judged, it would be judgment based on the testimony of one, which is not permissible, and because the claimant belied the witness of payment, which is a cause for disqualification. We say: he did not belie him concerning the first subject matter, the loan, but concerning what is against him, the payment, and that is not the same. Its like does not prevent acceptance. The conclusion is that the claimant's belying his witnesses is a cause for disqualification because it is voluntary, but his belying the defendant is not disqualification due to necessity of self-defense. (Ayni, Fath, Inayah) On the loan, due to complete proof; and not accepted on the payment due to lack thereof. (Ayni) Both rejected: [i.e., both testimonies; because one of the two groups is definitely lying, and neither is more deserving of acceptance than the other. (Ayni)] Because disagreement of witnesses on place prevents acceptance. If two witnesses testify that he killed in Mecca, and two others that he killed in Egypt, before the qadi gives judgment on the first testimony, he does not accept both; because killing cannot be in two places. Similarly, if they differ on time or the instrument of killing. The author did not mention the disagreement on time or place. The principle is: if the subject matter is a statement like sale and the like, disagreement of witnesses does not prevent acceptance; because statements can be repeated in times and places. If it is an act like usurpation, killing, etc., or a statement where an act is a condition of validity like marriage (which is a statement but presence of witnesses is a condition), then disagreement prevents acceptance; because an act in one time or place is different from an act in another time or place, so the subject matter differs. The scholar al-Maqdisi collected in his statement what makes disagreement in time or place a prevention of acceptance.
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings. The first revisits the loan-payment scenario but now from the perspective that the testimony of the loan is valid even if one witness adds payment; the payment part is not accepted because it is based on incomplete proof. The second ruling deals with a homicide case: one set of witnesses says the killing occurred in Mecca on Eid al-Adha, another set says in Egypt on the same day. Since the same act cannot occur in two different places at the same time, both testimonies are rejected as one must be false. This is because the subject matter is a physical act, and disagreement on place or time changes the act itself. The text then elaborates a general principle: for statements (e.g., contracts), disagreement on place/time does not invalidate because statements can be repeated. For acts, it does invalidate. Even for statements that require an act (e.g., marriage requires witnesses' presence), disagreement on place/time of that act invalidates the testimony. The passage ends with a reference to a poetic summary by al-Maqdisi, though the verse is not fully quoted in the OCR.

Key Terms
مشهود به (mashhūd bihī): The subject matter of the testimony – what the witnesses are testifying about.
اختلاف الشاهدين (ikhtilāf al-shāhidayn): Disagreement between witnesses on key facts of the case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two witnesses testify that a man committed theft in Baghdad, and two others that he committed the same theft in Basra on the same day. The testimonies are:
A) Both accepted, and the judge chooses one
B) Both rejected because a single theft cannot occur in two places
C) Accepted as long as the witnesses are upright
D) Only the first testimony is accepted

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, disagreement among witnesses on the time or place of a physical act invalidates all testimonies, but disagreement on the time or place of a statement does not.
