باب الاختلاف في الشهادة
ولهذا بألف. ملك المورث لم يُقض الوارثه بلا جرّ، إلا أن يشهدا بملكه أو يده استحساناً عنده خلافاً لهما
صورته: إذا ثبت شيء أنه ملك المورث بأن ادعى إنسان عيناً في يد إنسان أنها ميراث أبيه، وأقام شاهدين، فشهدا أن هذه كانت لأبيه، لا يقضى له بلا جرّ بأن يقول الشاهدان: إنها كانت لأبيه الذي مات وتركها ميراثاً له عند الطرفين، وقال أبو يوسف: الجر ليس بشرط، بل إذا أثبت الوارث أن العين كانت للمورث، يكفي؛ لأن ملك الميت قد ثبت بقول الشهود أنها كانت له، وملك الوارث خلافة عنه، ولهذا يرد بالعيب، ويرد عليه، ويصير مغروراً فيما اشتراه المورث. ولهما: أن ملك الوارث متجدد ثبت له بعد أن لم يكن ألا ترى أنه ثبت في حقه أحكام لم تكن ثابتة في حق المورث من استبراء الجارية وحل وطئها لو كانت حراماً على المورث أو بالعكس، ولو لا تجدد الملك لما حل له، فإذا كان الملك متجدداً فلابد من إثبات النقل إليه، ولابد مع الجر من بيان سبب الوراثة، فإذا شهدوا أنه أخوه، بيان أنه أخوه لأبيه وأمه أو لأحدهما، ومن شرط قبول الشهادة بالميراث: أن يدرك الشاهد الميت، وأن يقول: لا وارث له غيره، أو لا أعلم له وارثاً غيره وإلا فهي باطلة؛ لعدم معاينة السبب، وقيد بالملك؛ لأن إثبات شراء الوارث لا يتوقف على الجر.
فلابد من هو
إلا أن يشهدا بملكه أي ملك المورث، لا يقضى للوارث بلاجر في كل حال إلا في هذه الصور، منها: أن يشهد الشاهدان بملك المورث بأن يقولا: كانت لأبيه يوم موته؛ لأنه إذا ثبت ملكه وقت الموت كان جراً ضرورة،
أو يد مودعه أو مستعيره وقت الموت، ولو شهدا بيد حي مذ شهر، ردّت، ولو أقرّ المدعى عليه بذلك، أو شهد شاهدان أنه أقر أنه كان في يد المدعي، دفع إلى المدعي.
ولو قالا: كانت لأبيه، ولم يزدا على ذلك، لم يكن جراً، ومنها: أن يشهدا أنها كانت في يده عند الموت؛ لأن فيه جراً أيضاً؛ إذ يده إن كانت يد ملك عند الموت، فظاهر، وإن كانت يد أمانة فكذلك الحكم؛ لأن الأيدي في الأمانات عند الموت تنقلب يد ملك بواسطة الضمان إذا مات مجهلاً، والمضمون يملكه الضامن على ما عرف، فيكون إثبات اليد في ذلك الوقت إثباتاً للملك.
ومنها: أن يشهدا أنها كانت في يد مودعه أو مستعيره وكذا مستأجره ومرتهنه وغاصبه؛ لأن إثبات يد من يقوم مقامه إثبات ليده معنى فيغني إثبات الملك وقت الموت عن ذكر الجر، فاكتفى به عنه، وبيانه إذا مات رجل، فأقام وارثه بينة على دار أنها كانت لأبيه، أعارها أو آجرها أو أودعها أو رهنها أو غصبها الذي في يده، فإنه يأخذها، ولا يكلف البينة على ذكر الجر بأنه مات وتركها ميراثاً له، وهذه المسائل المستثناة بالإجماع.
ولو شهدا بيد حي إلخ [ أي الاثنان أن هذه العين كانت في يد شخص حي. ] شهدا أنه كان في يد المدعي منذ شهر، والحال أنه ليس في يد المدعي عند الدعوى، لا تقبل؛ لأن الشهادة قامت بمجهول؛ لأن اليد متنوعة إلى يد ملك ويد أمانة فتعذر القضاء بالمجهول، بخلاف الملك؛ فإنه معلوم غير متنوع، هذا عند الطرفين، وعند أبي يوسف تقبل؛ لأن اليد مقصودة كالملك، ولو شهدا أنه ملكه، تقبل، فكذا هنا، وقيد بالحي؛ لأنهما إذا شهدا للميت أنها كانت في يده وقت الموت، تقبل اتفاقاً، والمصنف أتى بهذه المسألة استطراداً ليست من باب الميراث.
وصورته: إذا كانت الدار في يد رجل فادعى آخر أنها له وأقام بينة أنها كانت في يده، والتقييد بقوله: "مذ شهر" لا حاجة إليه؛ فإنه ذكر "التمرتاشي" في "الجامع": شهدوا لحي أن العين كانت في يده، لم تقبل، فعلم أن الخلاف ثابت أيضاً بدون ذكره.
ردت أي هذه الشهادة عند الطرفين بذلك أي باليد للحي بأن العين كانت في يده.
دفع إلى المدعي لأنه تصح الشهادة بالإقرار فإنه معلوم وجهالة المقر به لا تمنع صحة الإقرار ألا ترى أنه لو قال لفلان على شيء صح، ويجب عليه البيان، ولا تصح الشهادة به، وإنما قال: "دفع إليه دون أن يقول : إنه إقرار بالملك له؛ لأنه لو برهن أنه ملكه يقبل، ولو قال: إنه كان بيده بغير حق ففيه خلاف والمفتى به أنه إقرار.
Chapter of Disagreement in Testimony. And for this, with a thousand. The property of the deceased is not adjudged to the heir without jarr (chain), unless they testify to his ownership or possession, by istihsan according to him, contrary to them (the Sahibayn). Its form: When it is established that something was the property of the deceased, such as a person claiming an object in someone's hand that it is his father's inheritance, and he produces two witnesses, and they testify that this belonged to his father, it is not adjudged to him without jarr, meaning the two witnesses say: it belonged to his father who died and left it as inheritance to him, according to the two sides. Abu Yusuf said: Jarr is not a condition; rather, if the heir proves that the object was the deceased's, it suffices, because the ownership of the deceased is established by the witnesses' statement that it belonged to him, and the heir's ownership is by succession from him, and for this it is returned due to defect, and returned upon him, and he becomes deceived in what the deceased purchased. And for them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): The heir's ownership is renewed, established for him after it was not. Do you not see that rulings are established in his right that were not established in the right of the deceased, such as istibra' of the slave-girl and permission of intercourse if she was forbidden to the deceased or vice versa; if ownership were not renewed, it would not be permitted for him. Since ownership is renewed, proof of transfer to him is necessary, and with jarr, explanation of the cause of inheritance is necessary. So if they testify that he is his brother, it must be clarified that he is his full brother or half-brother. Among the conditions for accepting testimony regarding inheritance is that the witness must have perceived the deceased, and must say: there is no other heir for him, or I know no other heir for him; otherwise it is invalid due to lack of direct observation of the cause. And it is restricted to ownership because proving the heir's purchase does not depend on jarr. Therefore, it is necessary [that] except that they testify to his ownership, i.e., the ownership of the deceased; the heir is not adjudged without jarr in any case except in these instances: including that the two witnesses testify to the deceased's ownership by saying: it belonged to his father on the day of his death; because if his ownership at the time of death is established, it is necessarily jarr; or the possession of his depositee or borrower at the time of death. And if they testify to a living person's possession since a month, it is rejected. And if the defendant acknowledged that, or two witnesses testified that he acknowledged that it was in the plaintiff's possession, it is handed over to the plaintiff. And if they said: it belonged to his father, and added nothing more, it is not jarr. And among them: that they testify that it was in his possession at death, because it also contains jarr; for if his possession was ownership possession at death, it is apparent; if it was amanah possession, the ruling is likewise, because possessory rights in trusts at death convert to ownership possession by virtue of guarantee (daman) if the deceased died without clear instructions, and the guaranteed item is owned by the guarantor as known; thus establishing possession at that time establishes ownership. And among them: that they testify that it was in the possession of his depositee, borrower, similarly lessee, pledgee, and usurper; because establishing possession of one who stands in his place is establishing his possession in meaning, so establishing ownership at the time of death suffices from mentioning jarr. Its explanation: When a man dies, and his heir brings evidence on a house that it belonged to his father, who loaned it, leased it, deposited it, pledged it, or it was usurped by the one in whose possession it is, then he takes it, and he is not required to bring evidence mentioning jarr that he died and left it as inheritance to him. These excepted cases are by consensus. And if they testify to a living person's possession, i.e., the two (witnesses) that this object was in the possession of a living person. They testified that it was in the plaintiff's possession since a month, while it is not in the plaintiff's possession at the time of claim, it is not accepted because the testimony is based on an unknown; since possession is divided into ownership possession and amanah possession, judgment on an unknown becomes impossible, unlike ownership, which is known and not divided. This is according to the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). According to Abu Yusuf, it is accepted because possession is intended like ownership; if they testified that it is his ownership, it is accepted, so here too. And it is restricted to a living person because if they testify for a deceased that it was in his possession at death, it is accepted by agreement. And the author brought this issue as a digression, not from the chapter of inheritance. Its form: When a house is in a man's possession and another claims it is his and brings evidence that it was in his possession, the restriction with 'since a month' is unnecessary, for al-Tamurtashi mentioned in al-Jami': they testified for a living person that the object was in his possession, it is not accepted; thus it is known that the disagreement is established without mentioning it. It is rejected, i.e., this testimony according to the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) due to that, i.e., due to possession of a living person that the object was in his possession. It is handed over to the plaintiff because testimony by acknowledgment is valid, for it is known, and ignorance of the thing acknowledged does not prevent validity of acknowledgment. Do you not see that if he said, 'So-and-so has something due from me,' it is valid, and he must clarify, but testimony by it is not valid. He said 'handed over to him' rather than saying it is acknowledgment of ownership, because if he proves it is his ownership, it is accepted; but if he says it was in his possession without right, there is disagreement, and the fatwa is that it is acknowledgment.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the requirement of jarr (chain of transfer) in testimony for inheritance. The author (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) states the basic ruling: when an heir claims property based on inheritance and produces witnesses that the property belonged to the deceased, the heir is not granted the property without jarr—meaning the witnesses must explicitly state that the deceased owned it and that it passed to the heir as inheritance. However, Abu Hanifa makes an exception by istihsan: if the witnesses testify to the deceased's ownership (e.g., saying 'it was his father's on the day of his death') or to possession (yad) at the time of death, that suffices without explicit jarr. Abu Yusuf argues that jarr is not a condition at all; proving the deceased's ownership is enough because the heir inherits from the deceased. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) respond that the heir's ownership is new (mutajaddid), not merely a continuation, as evidenced by different rulings applying to the heir (e.g., istibra' of a slave-girl), so transfer must be proven. The author then lists exceptions where jarr is unnecessary: when witnesses testify to ownership at death (necessarily implies transfer), or to possession (yad) of the deceased at death, or to possession of those who stood in his place (depositee, borrower, lessee, pledgee, usurper). The text also discusses testimony for possession of a living person, which is rejected due to ambiguity (possession could be ownership or amanah), though Abu Yusuf disagrees. Finally, testimony by acknowledgment (iqrar) is valid even if the thing acknowledged is unknown in detail, and handing over to the plaintiff is ordered. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) follows Abu Hanifa's istihsan excepting certain cases, and the condition of jarr is generally required per the Sahibayn's view which is more cautious.

Key Terms
جرّ (jarr): The requirement in testimony for inheritance that witnesses explicitly link the deceased's property to the heir as inheritance (e.g., 'it was his father's and he died leaving it to him').
ملك المورث (milk al-muwarrit): Ownership of the deceased; proving that the property belonged to the deceased at the time of death is key to inheritance claims.
يد (yad): Possession; testimony of possession at death can substitute for jarr because possession implies ownership unless proven otherwise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The witnesses state that the property was in the deceased's possession at death.
C) The witnesses state that the property was in a living person's possession.
D) The witnesses state that the property belonged to the deceased's father.

Key Takeaway
Jarr is required for inheritance testimony, but testimony to ownership or possession at death suffices by istihsan.

Shahadat — Testimony

Secondary Testimony: Accepted by Istihsan, Except in Hudud and Qisas
Explains the ruling and scope of accepting testimony upon testimony by istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on secondary testimony, explain the istihsan reasoning, and identify cases where it is not accepted (hudud/qisas) and those where it is (financial rights, waqf, ta'zir, lineage).

Core Idea
Secondary testimony is accepted by necessity but not where doubt itself nullifies the right.

This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling on shahada 'ala shahada (testimony upon testimony). While analogy (qiyas) would reject it because testimony is a physical act of worship, the school accepts it by istihsan (juristic preference) due to severe need. However, this acceptance has a key limitation: it does not apply in cases that are themselves nullified by doubt (shubha), namely hudud punishments and qisas. We will explore the reasoning, the inter-madhhab dispute, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi Ruling
State the Hanafi position: secondary testimony is accepted by istihsan in all matters except hudud and qisas.
2
Understand the Qiyas vs Istihsan
Analogy (qiyas) rejects secondary testimony because testimony is a physical act of worship that cannot be delegated. Istihsan overrides this due to necessity (haja) to prevent loss of rights.
3
Locate the Shubha Principle
Secondary testimony carries an element of substitution (shubhat al-badaliyyah). Therefore, it is not accepted where the case itself is nullified by doubt (shubha) – i.e., hudud and qisas.
4
Compare with Opposing Schools
The Three (Malik, Shafi‘i in one view, Hanbali in one narration) accept secondary testimony even in hudud and qisas. They argue that the need is equally present.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
In Hanafi law, hudud and qisas cannot be proven by secondary testimony. In Maliki/Shafi‘i law, they can. This difference affects how cases are adjudicated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(فتح، عيني)] جوازها استحسان، والقياس لا يقتضيه؛ لأن الأداء عبادة بدنية، لزمت الأصل لا حقاً للمشهود له؛ لعدم الإجبار، والإنابة لا تجري في العبادات البدنية، إلا أنهم استحسنوا جوازها في كل حق لا يسقط بالشبهة؛ لشدة الاحتياج إليها؛ لأن الأصل قد يعجز عن أدائها لبعض العوارض، فلو لم تجز لأدى إلى إتلاف الحقوق إلا أن فيها شبهة البدلية ولا يصار إلى البدل إلا عند العجز عن الأصل، وإذا ثبتت البدلية فيها لا تقبل فيما يسقط بالشبهات كشهادة النساء مع الرجال. (عيني)
Chapter of testimony upon testimony. It is accepted in [matters] that are not nullified by doubt, if two men testify to the testimony of two witnesses, i.e., in every right. Chapter of testimony [meaning: concerning the explanation of its rulings. When he finished from direct testimony, he began on secondary testimony, and the secondary is later than the original in existence, so he placed it later. (Fath, 'Ayni)] Its permissibility is by istihsan, and analogy does not require it, because performance is a physical act of worship, obligatory on the original not as a right of the beneficiary due to lack of compulsion, and delegation does not apply to physical acts of worship. However, they deemed it permissible by istihsan in every right that is not nullified by doubt, due to the severe need for it, because the original may be unable to perform it due to some impediments. If it were not permitted, it would lead to loss of rights. But in it there is an element of substitution, and substitution is resorted to only when unable to perform the original. When substitution is established in it, it is not accepted in matters nullified by doubts, like the testimony of women with men. ('Inayah, Fath) 'Accepted in [matters]...etc.' [meaning: testimony upon testimony by istihsan, and analogy would not accept it. (Ma'din)] Because in secondary testimony there is an element of substitution, so it is not permissible in matters nullified by doubt, namely hudud and qisas. According to the Three [schools], it is permissible in both as well, except in one opinion of al-Shafi'i and a narration from Ahmad. Al-Natifi mentioned that it is not permissible in waqf either, but the correct position is that it is permissible to revive it and preserve it from decay. It is permissible in ta'zir and lineage. ('Ayni, Fath, 'Inayah) 'By doubt' he guarded against hudud and qisas, because they are nullified by doubt, so it is not permissible in them. ('Ayni)
Source pages p. 468

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on testimony upon testimony (shahada 'ala shahada) is a ruling statement accompanied by its proof and an inter-madhhab dispute. The author begins by stating the Hanafi ruling: secondary testimony is accepted (by istihsan) in all matters that are not nullified by doubt (shubha). The proof is given: analogy (qiyas) would not accept it because testimony is a physical act of worship (ibada badaniyya) and cannot be delegated. However, due to necessity (haja), scholars practiced istihsan and accept secondary testimony in financial rights and other matters except those that are dropped by doubt (hudud and qisas). The element of substitution (shubhat al-badaliyyah) is present, so it cannot be used where doubt itself nullifies the entire case. The text then notes a disagreement: the three other schools (Maliki, Shafi'i in one view, and Hanbali in one narration) accept secondary testimony even in hudud and qisas. Additionally, al-Natifi mentioned that some do not accept it in waqf, but the correct Hanafi position is that it is accepted to protect the endowment from decay. Secondary testimony is also accepted in ta'zir (discretionary punishment) and lineage cases. The Hanafi school's reliance on the principle of shubha leads to this distinction.

Key Terms
شهادة على شهادة (shahāda ʿalā shahāda): Testimony upon testimony; a secondary witness testifies to the original witness's testimony.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a method of departing from analogy (qiyas) for a stronger reason, such as necessity.
شبهة (shubha): Doubt or ambiguity; a factor that can drop penalties (hudud, qisas) in Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following cases is secondary testimony (shahada 'ala shahada) NOT accepted according to the Hanafi school?
A) Financial rights
B) Waqf disputes
C) Hudud and qisas
D) Lineage cases

Key Takeaway
Secondary testimony is accepted by istihsan in all rights except hudud and qisas, due to the shubha principle.

Shahadat — Testimony

Requirement of Complete Nisab on Each Original Witness
Sets the condition that two witnesses must testify on each original witness's testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for valid secondary testimony and explain why the same two secondary witnesses can serve for multiple originals, distinguishing it from Shafi'i and other schools.

Core Idea
Each original witness's testimony requires its own complete nisab of secondary witnesses, but the same secondary witnesses can cover multiple originals.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq lays out the Hanafi ruling on the number of witnesses needed for secondary testimony (shahadah ala al-shahadah). The key condition is that each original witness must have a complete nisab of secondary witnesses testifying on his/her behalf. However, the Hanafi school permits the same pair of secondary witnesses to serve for multiple originals, a point of dispute with other madhhabs. In this lesson, you will learn the precise requirement, the proofs, and how the Hanafi position is defended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi Condition
The passage states that for secondary testimony to be valid, each original witness must have two men (or a man and two women) testify to their testimony.
The restriction to two men is not exclusive; women can be part of the nisab.
2
Understand the Application
The same two secondary witnesses can testify for multiple originals; they do not need to be distinct. Conversely, if each secondary witness testifies to only one original, it is invalid because each original lacks a complete nisab.
3
Examine the Opposing Views
Imam al-Shafi'i requires four distinct secondary witnesses (two for each original). Imam Ahmad allows one secondary to testify for both originals. Imam Malik allows one original to testify for another original.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Proof
A hadith from Ali (RA) is cited: 'The testimony of a man on the testimony of a man is not permitted except the testimony of two men.' The Hanafi school interprets this broadly without requiring distinct witnesses for each original.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning (dalala) is clear.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Response to Opposition
Hanafi response: Secondary testimony is a right (haqq) requiring a complete nisab, unlike hadith narration where a single reporter is accepted. Also, the secondary witness is a substitute (badal) and cannot be both original and secondary simultaneously.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن شهد رجلان [ أي إن شهد على شهادة كل واحد من الشاهدين الأصلين رجلان أو رجل وامرأتان. (عيني ط] أشار بهذا القول إلى شرط جواز الشهادة على الشهادة أي شرط جوازها: أن يشهد على شهادة كل واحد من الشاهدين الأصلين رجلان، وقيد الرجلين وقع اتفاقاً؛ لأنه يجوز أن يشهد على الشهادة رجل وامرأتان لتمام النصاب؛ لأن كل واحدة من الشاهدتين قضية من القضايا، فلابد من تمام النصاب على كل واحد منهما؛ ليثبت عند الحاكم ولا يشترط أن يكون المشهود على شهادته رجلا؛ لأن للمرأة أن تشهد على شهادتها رجلين أو رجلا وامرأتين ويجوز أن يشهد على شهادة كل امرأة نصاب الشهادة. وكذا لا يشترط تغاير الفروع، حتى لو أشهد أحدهما على شهادته رجلين، وأشهدهما الآخر بعينهما جاز، ولو شهد كل من الفرعين على شهادة كل واحد من الأصلين بانفراده، لا يجوز؛ لعدم النصاب في كل منهما، وكان القياس أن يكون شهود الفرع أربعة على كل شاهد من الأصل اثنان كما ذهب إليه الشافعي لله حتى قال: لا تجوز إلا أن يشهد على كل واحد منهما رجلان غير الذين أشهدهما صاحبه فيكون شهود الفرع أربعة؛ لأن الفرعين يقومان مقام أصل واحد، وعند أحمد: إذا شهد كل واحد من شهود الفرع على كل واحد من شهود الأصل، جاز. ولنا: ما روي عن علي الله أنه قال: "لا يجوز شهادة رجل على شهادة رجل إلا شهادة رجلين" مطلقاً من غير تقييد بأن يكون بإزاء كل رجل فرعان، ولأن الرجلين ينقلان شهادة الأصل، وهو من الحقوق، وقد تم على هذا نصاب الشهادة فيجوز أن يشهدا على الأصل الآخر أيضاً؛ لأن الشاهدين يجوز أن يشهدا في قضايا كثيرة. (عيني، فتح، عناية) ولا تقبل إلخ مستدرك بما قبله وإنما ذكره؛ لدفع توهم أن يراد بالمثنى المجموع، ولو شهد أحد الأصلين على آخر، لم يجز؛ لأن الأصالة تقتضي مشاهدة الحق والفرعية عدمها فيتنافيان، ولأن الفرع بدل عن الأصل، فلا يتصور أن يكون الشخص الواحد بدلاً وأصلاً في حالة واحدة، وعند مالك: تقبل، ونسب العيني هذا القول لأحمد؛ لأن الفرع معبر عن الأصل بمنزلة رسوله كرواية الأخبار، وبه قال الأوزاعي وابن أبي ليلى، ولنا: ما روينا عن علي وهو ظاهر الدلالة على المراد، ولأنه حق من الحقوق، فلابد من نصاب الشهادة، بخلاف رواية الأخبار فإنه من الدينيات، يقبل فيها خبر الواحد. (فتح، عناية)
If two men testify [i.e., if two men or a man and two women testify to the testimony of each of the two original witnesses. ('Ayni) He indicated by this statement the condition for the permissibility of testimony upon testimony, i.e., its condition: that two men testify to the testimony of each of the two original witnesses. The restriction to two men occurred by chance, because it is permissible for a man and two women to testify to the testimony, completing the nisab. Because each of the two [female] original witnesses is a case, so complete nisab is required on each of them to be established before the judge. It is not required that the one whose testimony is witnessed upon be a man, because a woman may have two men or a man and two women testify to her testimony, and it is permissible to have the nisab of testimony testify to each woman's testimony. Likewise, the change of secondary witnesses is not required, so that if one of them makes two men witnesses to his testimony, and the other makes the same two witnesses, it is permissible. If each of the secondary witnesses testifies to the testimony of each of the originals individually, it is not permissible due to lack of nisab in each. The analogy would be that the secondary witnesses are four, each original having two, as al-Shafi'i held, so he said: it is not permitted unless each of them has two men other than those made witnesses by his companion, so the secondary witnesses would be four, because the two secondary stand in place of one original. According to Ahmad: if each of the secondary witnesses testifies to each of the original witnesses, it is permissible. Our proof: what is narrated from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: 'The testimony of a man on the testimony of a man is not permitted except the testimony of two men,' absolutely without restriction that opposite each man there are two secondary witnesses. And because the two men convey the testimony of the original, which is one of the rights, and the nisab of testimony is complete on this basis, so they may testify to the other original as well, because the two witnesses may testify in many cases. ('Ayni, Fath, 'Inayah) 'And one is not accepted' etc. is appended to what preceded, and he mentioned it to refute the misconception that the dual [al-muthanna] refers to the aggregate. If one of the originals testifies for another, it is not permissible because originality requires direct observation of the right and secondary lacks it, so they are contradictory; and because the secondary is a substitute for the original, so it is inconceivable that one person be both substitute and original in one situation. According to Malik: it is accepted. Al-'Ayni attributed this statement to Ahmad, because the secondary is an interpreter of the original like his messenger, like the narration of hadith. And this was also said by al-Awza'i and Ibn Abi Layla. Our proof: what we narrated from Ali, which is clear evidence for what is intended, and because it is a right among rights, so the nisab of testimony is necessary, unlike the narration of hadith, because it is a religious matter, in which the report of one is accepted. (Fath, 'Inayah)
Source pages p. 468

Commentary
This passage addresses the condition of the number of witnesses required for secondary testimony. The Hanafi position is stated: two men (or a man and two women) must testify to the testimony of each original witness. The text clarifies that the restriction to two men in the phrase is not exclusive; women can also be secondary witnesses as part of the nisab. Importantly, the same two secondary witnesses can serve for both originals; they do not need to be distinct. However, if each secondary witness testifies to only one original individually, it is insufficient because each original's testimony lacks a complete nisab. The passage then presents a dispute. Imam al-Shafi'i requires four distinct secondary witnesses (two for each original). Imam Ahmad allows one secondary witness to testify on both originals if he testifies to each. The Hanafi proof is a narration from Ali (رضي الله عنه) that only two men can testify on one man's testimony. The Hanafi school also argues that testimony is a right (haqq) requiring a complete nisab, unlike hadith narration where a single report is accepted. The text also discusses a sub-issue: one original witness cannot testify on another original's testimony because he cannot be both original and secondary. Malik and others disagree, equating the secondary witness to a messenger. The Hanafi response relies on the same proof.

Key Terms
أصل (aṣl): Original witness who directly observed the fact and whose testimony is being conveyed.
فرع (farʿ): Secondary witness who testifies to the original's testimony, not directly to the fact.
نصاب الشهادة (niṣāb al-shahāda): The required number of witnesses to establish a case: two men or one man and two women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) No, each original needs distinct secondary witnesses.
B) Yes, the same two secondary witnesses can testify to both.
C) Yes, but only if the originals are men.
D) No, four secondary witnesses are required.

Key Takeaway
For secondary testimony to be valid in the Hanafi school, each original witness's testimony must be covered by a complete nisab of secondary witnesses, but the same secondary witnesses may serve for multiple originals.

The Procedure of Ishhad: Wording for Burdening and Performance
Describes the process of ishhad and the wording for burdening and performance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct wording for ishhad (burdening the secondary witness) and the wording for the secondary's performance in court, as per the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Ishhad is the formal transfer of testimony; the original says 'testify to my testimony' and the secondary conveys it.

In Hanafi law, secondary testimony (shahadah 'ala al-shahadah) requires a formal process called ishhad. The original witness must burden the secondary witness with a clear statement, and the secondary must then reproduce that in court. This lesson explains the required wordings.

Guided Path
1
Define ishhad and tahmil
Ishhad is the act of making someone a witness to one's own testimony. Tahmil is the burdening of the secondary witness with that testimony. Distinguish these from the performance (ada) of the secondary in court.
Tahmil is a necessary condition for the validity of secondary testimony.
2
Identify the wording of the original witness
The original must explicitly say something like: 'I testify that so-and-so acknowledged before me such-and-such, and I make you a witness to my testimony.' The key is to convey the testimony and assign the burden.
The wording can be in the form of a command: 'Bear witness to my testimony.'
3
Identify the wording of the secondary witness
The secondary says in court: 'I testify that so-and-so made me a witness to his testimony that so-and-so acknowledged before him such-and-such, and he said to me: Bear witness to my testimony to that.' This reproduces the burdening.
The secondary must repeat the original's exact testimony.
4
Understand that the wording must be explicit and can be adapted
While the core wording is fixed, variations are allowed as long as the meaning of tahmil and the testimony is clear. The text gives examples.
Ambiguity may invalidate the testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والإشهاد أن يقول: اشهد على شهادتي من الفرع أي كل واحد من الأصل أي صفة الإشهاد شاهد الأصل للفرع أني أشهد، وأن فلاناً أقرّ عندي بكذا، وأداء الفرع أن يقول: أشهد أن فلاناً أشهدني على شهادته أن فلاناً أقر عنده بكذا، وقال لي : اشهد على شهادتي بذلك. أي الأصل مع صاحبه الحق نصاب الشهادة فيجوز أن يشهدا على الأصل الآخر أيضاً؛ لأن الشاهدين يجوز أن يشهدا في قضايا كثيرة. (عيني، فتح، عناية) ولا تقبل إلخ مستدرك بما قبله وإنما ذكره؛ لدفع توهم أن يراد بالمثنى المجموع، ولو شهد أحد الأصلين على آخر، لم يجز؛ لأن الأصالة تقتضي مشاهدة الحق والفرعية عدمها فيتنافيان، ولأن الفرع بدل عن الأصل، فلا يتصور أن يكون الشخص الواحد بدلاً وأصلاً في حالة واحدة، وعند مالك: تقبل، ونسب العيني هذا القول لأحمد؛ لأن الفرع معبر عن الأصل بمنزلة رسوله كرواية الأخبار، وبه قال الأوزاعي وابن أبي ليلى، ولنا: ما روينا عن علي وهو ظاهر الدلالة على المراد، ولأنه حق من الحقوق، فلابد من نصاب الشهادة، بخلاف رواية الأخبار فإنه من الدينيات، يقبل فيها خبر الواحد. (فتح، عناية) والإشهاد إلخ: لأن الفرع كالنائب عنه، فلابد من التحميل والتوكيل، ولابد أن يشهد عنده كما يشهد عند القاضي؛ لينقله إلى مجلس القاضي، وإنما قالوا: الفرع كالنائب، ولم يجعلوه نائباً؛ لأن للقاضي أن يقضي بشهادة أصل وفرعين أصل آخر، ولو كان الفرع نائباً حقيقة لما جاز الجمع بين الأصل والخلف، وأجيب بعدم الجمع بينهما؛ لأن الفرعين ليسا ببدل عن الذي شهد معهما، بل عن الذي لم يحضر، ويقول الأصل للفرع عند التحميل: أشهدني على نفسه إن شاء وليس بلازم؛ لأن من عاين الحق له أن يشهد وإن لم يشهده على نفسه، ويكفي سكوت الفرع، ولو رده ارتد ولا ينبغي للفرع أن يشهد على شهادة من ليس بعدل عنده. (عيني، فتح) اشهد إلخ للشهادة لفظ أطول وأقصر لكن ذكر الوسط إلى العدل أقرب وخير الأمور أوساطها، أما الأطول فهو أن يقول الأصل: أشهد بكذا وأنا أشهدك على شهادتي فاشهد على شهادتي، وفيه خمس شينات، ويقول الفرع: أشهد أن فلاناً شهد عندي بكذا، وأشهدني على شهادته بذلك، وأمرني أن أشهد على شهادته، وأنا أشهد على شهادته بذلك فيه ثمان شينات. ومنهم من قال: يقول الفرع: أربع شينات، وهو أن يقول: أشهد أن فلاناً قال لي: اشهد على شهادتي، وأنا ومنهم من قال بثلاث شينات، وهو أن يقول: أشهد أن فلاناً قال لي : اشهد على شهادتي كذا، أو يقول: أشهد أن فلاناً أشهدني على شهادته بكذا، وذكر محمد في السير الكسير: بأقصر الأقوال أن يقول الفرع: أشهد على شهادة فلان أن فلاناً أقر بكذا، فيذكر فيه شينين لا غير، وهو اختيار الفقيه أبي الليث وأبي جعفر وشمس الأئمة السرخسي، وهو أسهل وأيسر. [ رمز الحقائق: ١٥٨/٢]
And the ishhad is that he says: 'Make me a witness to my testimony' from the secondary, i.e., each one of the original. i.e., the description of ishhad: the original witness says to the secondary: 'I testify, and so-and-so acknowledged before me such-and-such.' The performance of the secondary is to say: 'I testify that so-and-so made me a witness to his testimony that so-and-so acknowledged before him such-and-such, and he said to me: Bear witness to my testimony to that.' i.e., the original with his companion. The right [requires] the nisab of testimony, so it is permissible for them to testify to the other original as well, because the two witnesses may testify in many cases. ('Ayni, Fath, 'Inayah) 'And one is not accepted' etc. is appended to what preceded, and he mentioned it to refute the misconception that the dual refers to the aggregate. If one of the originals testifies for another, it is not permissible... (as above) (Fath, 'Inayah) 'And the ishhad' etc.: because the secondary is like a deputy for him, so burdening (tahmil) and authorization (tawkid) are necessary, and it is necessary that he testifies before him just as he testifies before the judge, to convey it to the court. They said the secondary is like a deputy, but they did not make him an actual deputy because the judge may rule based on the testimony of an original and two secondaries of another original. If the secondary were a true deputy, combining the original and the substitute would not be permissible. The answer is that there is no combination, because the two secondaries are not a substitute for the one who testified with them, but rather for the one who did not attend. The original says to the secondary at the time of burdening: 'Make me a witness to myself' if he wishes, but it is not necessary, because one who has witnessed the right may testify even if he did not make someone a witness to himself. The secondary's silence is sufficient; if he declines, he returns, and it is not proper for the secondary to testify to the testimony of one who is not just in his view. ('Ayni, Fath) 'Witness' etc.: For testimony there is a longer and a shorter wording, but the middle is closer to justice, and the best of things is their middle. As for the longest: the original says: 'I testify to such-and-such, and I make you a witness to my testimony, so testify to my testimony.' It contains five shins. The secondary says: 'I testify that so-and-so testified before me to such-and-such, and he made me a witness to his testimony to that, and he commanded me to testify to his testimony, and I testify to his testimony to that.' It contains eight shins. Some said: the secondary says four shins: 'I testify that so-and-so said to me: testify to my testimony, and I...' Some said three shins: 'I testify that so-and-so said to me: testify to my testimony such-and-such,' or 'I testify that so-and-so made me a witness to his testimony such-and-such.' Muhammad mentioned in al-Siyar al-Kabir: the shortest wording is that the secondary says: 'I testify to the testimony of so-and-so that so-and-so acknowledged such-and-such,' thus mentioning only two shins. This is the choice of Faqih Abu al-Layth, Abu Ja'far, and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, and it is the easiest and simplest. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/158]
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage explains the procedural aspects of making a secondary witness (ishhad) and the wording used by the original and secondary witnesses. The original witness must formally burden (tahmil) the secondary witness by saying something like 'I testify to such-and-such, make me a witness to my testimony.' The secondary witness then conveys this in court. The text discusses various lengths of wording, measured by the number of times the letter 'shin' appears in the Arabic word 'ashhad' (I testify). The longest wording has five shins for the original and eight for the secondary. The shortest, chosen by Imam Muhammad, Faqih Abu al-Layth, and Imam Sarakhsi, is for the secondary to say: 'I testify to the testimony of so-and-so that so-and-so acknowledged such-and-such,' containing only two shins. This is considered the easiest. The passage also clarifies that the secondary is like a deputy (na'ib) but not an actual deputy, because a judge can combine the testimony of an original and secondaries of another original, which cannot happen with true substitution. The original does not need to force the secondary to accept the burden; silence suffices. The secondary should only testify if he considers the original to be just ('adl).

Key Terms
إشهاد (ishhād): The act of making someone a witness to one's own testimony; the process of burdening a secondary witness.
تحميل (taḥmīl): The burdening of the secondary witness with the testimony; the original witness formally assigns his testimony to the secondary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 'I testify to such-and-such.'
B) 'Bear witness to my testimony.'
C) 'Tell the judge what I told you.'
D) Both A and B are required.

Key Takeaway
Ishhad requires the original to explicitly burden the secondary with a clear statement of testimony, and the secondary must reproduce that statement in court.

Lengths of Testimony Wording: The 'Shin' Count
Discusses various wordings for secondary testimony based on shin count

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the longest, medium, and shortest wordings for secondary testimony based on the count of the letter 'shin' in 'ashhad', and state the preferred shortest wording.

Core Idea
The wording for secondary testimony can vary from 2 to 8 shins; the shortest (2 shins) is the easiest and chosen by leading Hanafi scholars.

Hanafi jurists analyzed the wording of secondary testimony by counting the occurrences of the letter 'shin' in the word 'ashhad' (I testify). This lesson walks through the longest (8 shins), a medium (3-5 shins), and the shortest (2 shins) wording, and explains why the shortest is preferred for ease.

Guided Path
1
Identify the metric: the 'shin' count
The letter 'shin' (ش) appears each time the word 'ashhad' is used. Counting shins measures the length and complexity of the wording.
This is a technical convenience, not a legal requirement.
2
Examine the longest wording (8 shins)
The longest wording for the secondary includes multiple 'ashhad' statements: 'أشهد أن فلاناً شهد عندي بكذا، وأشهدني على شهادته بذلك، وأمرني أن أشهد على شهادته، وأنا أشهد على شهادته بذلك' – eight shins.
This is cumbersome and rarely used.
3
Examine intermediate wordings (3-5 shins)
Some scholars suggested shorter versions: the original says 5 shins, the secondary says 4 shins or 3 shins. For example, secondary: 'أشهد أن فلاناً قال لي: اشهد على شهادتي' (3 shins).
These are acceptable but not the shortest.
4
Identify the shortest wording (2 shins)
The shortest wording is narrated from Imam Muhammad in al-Siyar al-Kabir: the secondary says: 'أشهد على شهادة فلان أن فلاناً أقر بكذا' – only two shins. This is the choice of Faqih Abu al-Layth, Abu Ja'far, and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi.
Imam al-Sarakhsi considered it the easiest and simplest.
5
Understand the preference for ease
The Hanafi school values ease in legal procedures. The shortest wording avoids verbosity while still clearly conveying the testimony and the chain of burdening.
This reflects the general principle: 'خير الأمور أوساطها' but here the shortest is preferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والإشهاد أن يقول: اشهد على شهادتي من الفرع أي كل واحد من الأصل أي صفة الإشهاد شاهد الأصل للفرع أني أشهد، وأن فلاناً أقرّ عندي بكذا، وأداء الفرع أن يقول: أشهد أن فلاناً أشهدني على شهادته أن فلاناً أقر عنده بكذا، وقال لي : اشهد على شهادتي بذلك. أي الأصل مع صاحبه الحق نصاب الشهادة فيجوز أن يشهدا على الأصل الآخر أيضاً؛ لأن الشاهدين يجوز أن يشهدا في قضايا كثيرة. (عيني، فتح، عناية) ولا تقبل إلخ مستدرك بما قبله وإنما ذكره؛ لدفع توهم أن يراد بالمثنى المجموع، ولو شهد أحد الأصلين على آخر، لم يجز؛ لأن الأصالة تقتضي مشاهدة الحق والفرعية عدمها فيتنافيان، ولأن الفرع بدل عن الأصل، فلا يتصور أن يكون الشخص الواحد بدلاً وأصلاً في حالة واحدة، وعند مالك: تقبل، ونسب العيني هذا القول لأحمد؛ لأن الفرع معبر عن الأصل بمنزلة رسوله كرواية الأخبار، وبه قال الأوزاعي وابن أبي ليلى، ولنا: ما روينا عن علي وهو ظاهر الدلالة على المراد، ولأنه حق من الحقوق، فلابد من نصاب الشهادة، بخلاف رواية الأخبار فإنه من الدينيات، يقبل فيها خبر الواحد. (فتح، عناية) والإشهاد إلخ: لأن الفرع كالنائب عنه، فلابد من التحميل والتوكيل، ولابد أن يشهد عنده كما يشهد عند القاضي؛ لينقله إلى مجلس القاضي، وإنما قالوا: الفرع كالنائب، ولم يجعلوه نائباً؛ لأن للقاضي أن يقضي بشهادة أصل وفرعين أصل آخر، ولو كان الفرع نائباً حقيقة لما جاز الجمع بين الأصل والخلف، وأجيب بعدم الجمع بينهما؛ لأن الفرعين ليسا ببدل عن الذي شهد معهما، بل عن الذي لم يحضر، ويقول الأصل للفرع عند التحميل: أشهدني على نفسه إن شاء وليس بلازم؛ لأن من عاين الحق له أن يشهد وإن لم يشهده على نفسه، ويكفي سكوت الفرع، ولو رده ارتد ولا ينبغي للفرع أن يشهد على شهادة من ليس بعدل عنده. (عيني، فتح) اشهد إلخ للشهادة لفظ أطول وأقصر لكن ذكر الوسط إلى العدل أقرب وخير الأمور أوساطها، أما الأطول فهو أن يقول الأصل: أشهد بكذا وأنا أشهدك على شهادتي فاشهد على شهادتي، وفيه خمس شينات، ويقول الفرع: أشهد أن فلاناً شهد عندي بكذا، وأشهدني على شهادته بذلك، وأمرني أن أشهد على شهادته، وأنا أشهد على شهادته بذلك فيه ثمان شينات. ومنهم من قال: يقول الفرع: أربع شينات، وهو أن يقول: أشهد أن فلاناً قال لي: اشهد على شهادتي، وأنا ومنهم من قال بثلاث شينات، وهو أن يقول: أشهد أن فلاناً قال لي : اشهد على شهادتي كذا، أو يقول: أشهد أن فلاناً أشهدني على شهادته بكذا، وذكر محمد في السير الكسير: بأقصر الأقوال أن يقول الفرع: أشهد على شهادة فلان أن فلاناً أقر بكذا، فيذكر فيه شينين لا غير، وهو اختيار الفقيه أبي الليث وأبي جعفر وشمس الأئمة السرخسي، وهو أسهل وأيسر. [ رمز الحقائق: ١٥٨/٢]
And the ishhad is that he says: 'Make me a witness to my testimony' from the secondary, i.e., each one of the original. i.e., the description of ishhad: the original witness says to the secondary: 'I testify, and so-and-so acknowledged before me such-and-such.' The performance of the secondary is to say: 'I testify that so-and-so made me a witness to his testimony that so-and-so acknowledged before him such-and-such, and he said to me: Bear witness to my testimony to that.' i.e., the original with his companion. The right [requires] the nisab of testimony, so it is permissible for them to testify to the other original as well, because the two witnesses may testify in many cases. ('Ayni, Fath, 'Inayah) 'And one is not accepted' etc. is appended to what preceded, and he mentioned it to refute the misconception that the dual refers to the aggregate. If one of the originals testifies for another, it is not permissible... (as above) (Fath, 'Inayah) 'And the ishhad' etc.: because the secondary is like a deputy for him, so burdening (tahmil) and authorization (tawkid) are necessary, and it is necessary that he testifies before him just as he testifies before the judge, to convey it to the court. They said the secondary is like a deputy, but they did not make him an actual deputy because the judge may rule based on the testimony of an original and two secondaries of another original. If the secondary were a true deputy, combining the original and the substitute would not be permissible. The answer is that there is no combination, because the two secondaries are not a substitute for the one who testified with them, but rather for the one who did not attend. The original says to the secondary at the time of burdening: 'Make me a witness to myself' if he wishes, but it is not necessary, because one who has witnessed the right may testify even if he did not make someone a witness to himself. The secondary's silence is sufficient; if he declines, he returns, and it is not proper for the secondary to testify to the testimony of one who is not just in his view. ('Ayni, Fath) 'Witness' etc.: For testimony there is a longer and a shorter wording, but the middle is closer to justice, and the best of things is their middle. As for the longest: the original says: 'I testify to such-and-such, and I make you a witness to my testimony, so testify to my testimony.' It contains five shins. The secondary says: 'I testify that so-and-so testified before me to such-and-such, and he made me a witness to his testimony to that, and he commanded me to testify to his testimony, and I testify to his testimony to that.' It contains eight shins. Some said: the secondary says four shins: 'I testify that so-and-so said to me: testify to my testimony, and I...' Some said three shins: 'I testify that so-and-so said to me: testify to my testimony such-and-such,' or 'I testify that so-and-so made me a witness to his testimony such-and-such.' Muhammad mentioned in al-Siyar al-Kabir: the shortest wording is that the secondary says: 'I testify to the testimony of so-and-so that so-and-so acknowledged such-and-such,' thus mentioning only two shins. This is the choice of Faqih Abu al-Layth, Abu Ja'far, and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, and it is the easiest and simplest. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/158]
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage explains the procedural aspects of making a secondary witness (ishhad) and the wording used by the original and secondary witnesses. The original witness must formally burden (tahmil) the secondary witness by saying something like 'I testify to such-and-such, make me a witness to my testimony.' The secondary witness then conveys this in court. The text discusses various lengths of wording, measured by the number of times the letter 'shin' appears in the Arabic word 'ashhad' (I testify). The longest wording has five shins for the original and eight for the secondary. The shortest, chosen by Imam Muhammad, Faqih Abu al-Layth, and Imam Sarakhsi, is for the secondary to say: 'I testify to the testimony of so-and-so that so-and-so acknowledged such-and-such,' containing only two shins. This is considered the easiest. The passage also clarifies that the secondary is like a deputy (na'ib) but not an actual deputy, because a judge can combine the testimony of an original and secondaries of another original, which cannot happen with true substitution. The original does not need to force the secondary to accept the burden; silence suffices. The secondary should only testify if he considers the original to be just ('adl).

Key Terms
شين (shīn): The letter 'shin'; used to count the number of times the word 'ashhad' (I testify) appears in the wording.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the shortest acceptable wording for a secondary witness?
A) أشهد أن فلاناً شهد عندي بكذا
B) أشهد على شهادة فلان أن فلاناً أقر بكذا
C) أشهد أن فلاناً قال لي: اشهد على شهادتي
D) أشهد أن فلاناً أشهدني على شهادته بكذا

Key Takeaway
The shortest wording for secondary testimony (2 shins) is the easiest and preferred in the Hanafi school, though longer wordings are also valid.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
7 min
Legal Nature of the Secondary Witness: Deputy but Not Substitute
Explains the legal nature of the secondary witness as a deputy and related rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the secondary witness is considered a deputy (na'ib) rather than a substitute (badal), and state the rulings that follow from this distinction, including the prohibition of one original testifying for another and the condition of justice.

Core Idea
The secondary witness is a deputy conveying testimony, not a substitute; thus, one original cannot be a secondary for another original, and the secondary must ensure the original is just.

The Hanafi school draws a careful distinction regarding the role of the secondary witness: he is like a deputy (na'ib) who conveys the original's testimony, but not a full substitute. This distinction has practical consequences: a judge may combine the testimony of an original with secondaries from another original, and one original cannot testify for another original. Additionally, the secondary must only testify if he deems the original to be just ('adl). This lesson explores these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Understand the 'deputy but not substitute' concept
The secondary is like a deputy (na'ib) because he conveys the original's testimony. However, he is not a true substitute (badal) because the originals remain the primary witnesses. Evidence: a judge can rule based on an original and two secondaries of another original – true substitution would not allow combining.
The rationale: the secondaries are not substituting for the original who is present but for the absent original.
2
Rule: One original cannot testify for another
If one original witness testifies as a secondary for another original, it is not permitted (la yajuz). Reason: originality requires direct observation of the right, while being a secondary implies lack thereof – they are mutually exclusive. A person cannot be both original and secondary in the same case.
Also, the secondary is a 'badal' (substitute) for the original, and one person cannot be both original and substitute simultaneously.
3
Condition: The secondary must consider the original just
It is not proper for the secondary to testify if he does not consider the original to be just ('adl). The secondary can remain silent; if he refuses, he is not compelled. The original does not have to force acceptance.
This is based on the principle that testimony is a religious duty that should not be performed if tainted.
4
Practical implications in court
The judge may combine the testimony of an original witness with secondaries of another original. This is allowed because the secondaries are not substitutes for the original present but for the absent one. This harmonizes the roles.
This solves the apparent contradiction in the deputy role.

Commentary
This passage explains the procedural aspects of making a secondary witness (ishhad) and the wording used by the original and secondary witnesses. The original witness must formally burden (tahmil) the secondary witness by saying something like 'I testify to such-and-such, make me a witness to my testimony.' The secondary witness then conveys this in court. The text discusses various lengths of wording, measured by the number of times the letter 'shin' appears in the Arabic word 'ashhad' (I testify). The longest wording has five shins for the original and eight for the secondary. The shortest, chosen by Imam Muhammad, Faqih Abu al-Layth, and Imam Sarakhsi, is for the secondary to say: 'I testify to the testimony of so-and-so that so-and-so acknowledged such-and-such,' containing only two shins. This is considered the easiest. The passage also clarifies that the secondary is like a deputy (na'ib) but not an actual deputy, because a judge can combine the testimony of an original and secondaries of another original, which cannot happen with true substitution. The original does not need to force the secondary to accept the burden; silence suffices. The secondary should only testify if he considers the original to be just ('adl).

Key Terms
بدل (badal): Substitute; the secondary is considered a substitute for the original in the sense of representing him, but not a full legal substitute.
نائب (nā'ib): Deputy; the secondary is like a deputy conveying testimony, but not an actual deputy (na'ib haqiqi) because of the ability to combine with original.
عدل ('adl): Just; a quality required for all witnesses. The secondary must consider the original just.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi school, why is it impermissible for one original witness to testify as a secondary for another original?
A) Because the secondary must be absent from the event.
B) Because originality requires direct observation, which contradicts the secondary's role.
C) Because the nisab of testimony would be incomplete.
D) Because the original would be biased.

Key Takeaway
The secondary witness is a deputy conveying testimony, not a substitute, and therefore one original cannot act as a secondary for another, and the secondary must personally deem the original just.

Conditions for Secondary Testimony and Extended Excuses
Ruling on conditions for secondary testimony with extended excuses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid secondary testimony (shahada 'ala shahada) and identify which excuses for the original witness are sufficient according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Secondary testimony is valid only when the original witness cannot attend court — and the excuse is not limited to death, illness, or travel.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq discusses the rules for testimony based on another's testimony (shahada 'ala shahada). It clarifies that secondary testimony is permitted only when the original witness has a valid excuse, and it expands the recognized excuses beyond the three commonly mentioned. Understanding these conditions is crucial for ensuring that testimony is accepted in court while protecting the rights of litigants.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three basic excuses
The matn lists death, illness, and travel of the original witness as the classic excuses that permit secondary testimony. Recognize these as the starting point.
These are examples, not exhaustive.
2
Understand the underlying principle
The permissibility of secondary testimony is based on the need (haja) when the original witness is unable to attend court. This principle justifies the expansion of excuses.
The proof is talil (rational reasoning) from necessity.
3
Recognize the expansion of excuses
The commentary explicitly states that the excuse is not limited to the three. Examples include a woman in seclusion (mukhaddarah) and, according to Abu Yusuf, a person who cannot return home overnight if they attend court.
This is the mufta bihi position.
4
Apply the correct wording for transmission
The original must say 'ashhad 'ala shahadati' (bear witness upon my testimony) and not ambiguous phrases like 'ashhad 'ala hadha', which could imply testifying to the fact itself.
The secondary's wording at performance also has a preferred form (five 'shin' letters).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الشهادة على الشهادة
ولا شهادة للفرع بلا موت أصله أو مرضه أو سفره، فإن عدلهم الفروع صح، مقبولة أي أصل الفرع الأصول وهكذا الأقصر في تحميل الشهادة من الأصل للفرع أن يقول :الأصل: اشهد أنت على شهادتي بكذا، ولا يقول الأصل: اشهد علي بكذا؛ لأنه لفظ محتمل يحتمل أن يكون الإشهاد على نفس الحق المشهود به فيكون أمرا بالكذب وكذا لا يقول اشهد بشهادتي، وما ذكره في المتن من قول الفرع عند الأداء بخمس شينات اختيار شمس الأئمة الحلواني، وهو أحسن فيما ذكروه. (فتح) ولا شهادة إلخ: لأن جوازها للحاجة عند عجز الأصل، والعجز يتحقق بهذه الأشياء، والمعنى لا تقبل شهادة الفرع عند القاضي، ونفس الإشهاد يجوز وإن لم يكن بالأصل عذر، والمراد بالموت الموت الحكمي لا الموت الحقيقي؛ لأن شهادة الفرع تبطل بموت الأصل حقيقة، وليس العذر منحصرا في هذه الأشياء الثلاثة، بل إذا كانت الأصل امرأة مخدرة يجوز لها أن تشهد على شهادتها، وهي التي لم تخالط الرجال ولو خرجت لقضاء حاجة أو حمام، وعن أبي يوسف الله: أنه لو كان الأصل في مكان لو غدا لأداء الشهادة لا يقدر أن يبيت في منزله، جاز الإشهاد إحياء لحقوق الناس، وعليه أكثر المشايخ، وعليه الفتوى.
Chapter of Testimony upon Testimony. And there is no testimony of the secondary witness without the death of his original witness, or his illness, or his travel. If the secondary witnesses modify the original witnesses, it is valid. 'Accepted' meaning the original of the secondary witness, the originals. And thus the shortest in the transmission of testimony from the original to the secondary is that the original says: 'Bear witness you upon my testimony of such-and-such,' and the original should not say: 'Bear witness upon this,' because it is a word that is probabilistic, possibly meaning the witness is upon the very right being witnessed, thus it would be a command to lie. Similarly, he should not say: 'Bear witness with my testimony.' And what is mentioned in the text about the statement of the secondary witness at the time of performance with five sin letters (shin) is the choice of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, and it is best according to what they mentioned. (Fath) 'And there is no testimony... etc.' because its permissibility is due to need when the original is unable, and inability is realized by these things. The meaning is that the testimony of the secondary is not accepted before the judge, but the act of transmission itself is permissible even if there is no excuse for the original. And by death is meant legal death, not actual death, because the testimony of the secondary is invalidated by the actual death of the original. The excuse is not limited to these three things. Rather, if the original is a woman in seclusion, it is permissible for her to testify upon her testimony; she is one who does not mix with men, even if she goes out for a need or to the bath. And from Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) that if the original was in a place such that if he were to go in the morning to perform the testimony, he would not be able to return to his home at night, then the transmission is permitted to revive people's rights. Upon this opinion are most of the mashayikh, and upon it is the fatwa.
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq on the conditions for the validity of secondary testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada). The matn states three specific excuses that permit secondary testimony: death, illness, and travel of the original witness. The commentary expands that these are not exhaustive; any valid inability qualifies. It also specifies that the secondary witness's testimony is only accepted when the original cannot attend court, but the act of transmitting the testimony is permissible even without an excuse. The commentary extends the excuses to include a woman in seclusion (mukhaddarah) and, according to Abu Yusuf, a situation where attending court would prevent the original from returning home for the night. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Yusuf. The passage also provides guidance on the precise wording for transmission: the original should say 'Bear witness upon my testimony' not 'Bear witness upon this' to avoid ambiguity.

Key Terms
أصل (asl): The original witness whose testimony is being transmitted
فرع (far'): The secondary witness who transmits the testimony of the original
شهادة على شهادة (shahada 'ala shahada): Testimony of a secondary witness based on the testimony of an original witness

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum condition for the validity of secondary testimony (shahada 'ala shahada)?
A) The original witness must be dead.
B) The original witness must be ill.
C) The original witness must be unable to attend court due to any valid excuse.
D) The original witness must have traveled at least three days journey.

Key Takeaway
Secondary testimony is allowed when the original witness cannot attend court, and the excuse is not limited to death, illness, or travel—any valid inability suffices, according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Secondary Testimony Without Excuse: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Location
Intra-Hanafi dispute on secondary testimony and the analogy with tawkeel.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on secondary testimony when the original witness is in the same city without excuse, and explain the basis of the analogy with deputation in litigation.

Core Idea
The validity of secondary testimony without excuse depends on whether deputation in litigation is allowed without consent.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute: when the original witness is in the same city but does not appear in court, can a secondary witness testify on his behalf? The answer hinges on a deeper question about the permissibility of deputation in litigation. We will explore the positions of Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), and see how qiyas and istihsan shape their rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the positions
The issue is whether secondary testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada) is valid when the original witness is present in the same city (misr) but has no specific excuse not to attend court. State Abu Hanifa's view (invalid) and the Sahibayn's view (valid).
This is purely an intra-Hanafi disagreement.
2
Understand Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa uses qiyas (analogy) with deputation in litigation (tawkeel bil khusuma). Just as a defendant cannot appoint a representative without the opponent's consent or an excuse, the original witness cannot deputize a secondary witness without an excuse.
The analogy treats the act of providing testimony as a personal obligation that cannot be delegated.
3
Understand the Sahibayn's proof
The two companions rely on istihsan (juristic preference) based on necessity and the principle of reviving rights (ihya' huquq al-nas). They allow deputation in litigation without consent, and by extension, secondary testimony without excuse.
Their view facilitates the enforcement of rights when the original witness is available but not present.
4
Analyze the analogy
The link (jihah) between tawkeel and secondary testimony is the delegation of a legal act to another. Abu Hanifa sees the absence of consent/excuse as decisive; the Sahibayn see the necessity of preserving rights as overriding.
This is a classic example of qiyas khafi versus istihsan.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical consequence: according to Abu Hanifa, secondary testimony is rejected; according to the Sahibayn, it is accepted. The fatwa is according to the Sahibayn, as noted in al-Nihaya, because their view is more practical and followed by later mashayikh.
The mufta bihi is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن محمد: أنها يجوز كيف ما كان، حتى روي عنه: أنه إذا كان الأصل في زاوية المسجد، فشهد الفرع على شهادته بزاوية أخرى من ذلك المسجد، تقبل شهادتهم، وفي 'النهاية' عن السرخسي والسغدي: إذا شهد الفروع على شهادة الأصول، والأصول في المصر، يجب أن تجوز على قولهما، وعلى قول أبي حنيفة لا يجوز بناء على أن التوكيل بالخصومة بغير رضا الخصم لا يجوز عنده وعندهما يجوز، وجه البناء: أن المدعى عليه لا يملك إنابة غيره مناب نفسه في الجواب لا بعذر فكذا لا يملك الأصل إنابة غيره مناب نفسه إلا بعذر.
And from Muhammad: that it is permissible in any case, even if the original is in one corner of the mosque and the secondary testifies in another corner, their testimony is accepted. And in al-Nihaya from al-Sarakhsi and al-Sughdi: If the secondary witnesses testify upon the testimony of the originals, and the originals are in the city, it must be permissible according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), but according to Abu Hanifa it is not permissible, based on the fact that deputation in litigation without the consent of the opponent is not permissible according to him, but according to the two it is permissible. The basis of the construction is that the defendant does not have the right to deputize another in his place for the response without an excuse, so likewise the original witness does not have the right to deputize another in his place except with an excuse.
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether secondary testimony is valid when the original witness is present in the same city but does not attend court. According to a narration from Muhammad al-Shaybani, it is permissible in all cases, even if the original is in the same mosque. The text then cites al-Nihaya, which states that according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, if the originals are in the city, it is permissible; but according to Abu Hanifa, it is not, because he analogizes it to deputation in litigation (tawkeel bil khusuma), which is not allowed without the opponent's consent. The reasoning is that just as the defendant cannot appoint someone else to respond in court without an excuse, the original witness cannot appoint a secondary witness without an excuse. The two companions (Sahibayn) disagree, allowing deputation, and thus allow secondary testimony even without excuse. The dispute is purely within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
توكيل بالخصومة (tawkeel bil khusuma): Deputation to represent in litigation
شهادة على الشهادة (shahada 'ala al-shahada): Secondary testimony, where a witness testifies to the testimony of another witness

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the basis for Abu Hanifa's position that secondary testimony is not valid when the original is in the city without excuse?
A) Because the secondary witness is not reliable.
B) Because it is analogous to deputation in litigation without consent.
C) Because the original witness must be present in court.
D) Because the secondary witness might be lying.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of secondary testimony without excuse is a contested issue within the Hanafi school, with the fatwa favoring the Sahibayn's position based on istihsan.

Modification and Nullification of Secondary Testimony
Rulings on mutual modification and nullification of secondary testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules on modification and nullification of secondary testimony, distinguishing the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Core Idea
Secondary testimony is nullified if the original denies; Abu Yusuf allows judge to investigate if secondary is silent.

Secondary testimony (shahadat ala al-shahada) is a unique institution in Islamic evidence law. This lesson unpacks the rules for modifying the reliability of original witnesses and the conditions that nullify secondary testimony. You will learn the mutual modification process and a key intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether secondary witnesses must always certify the original's reliability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core rule on mutual modification
The passage begins by stating that secondary witnesses can modify the originals and vice versa. Understand that after transmission, the secondary becomes a third party, so his modification is valid.
This reciprocity is based on the idea that both are capable of judging reliability after the relationship ends.
2
Distinguish scenarios of judge's knowledge
If the judge knows both groups by reliability, he proceeds with the testimony. If he knows only one, he asks about the unknown. This determines when modification is needed.
The judge's personal knowledge obviates the need for formal modification.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute on secondary's duty to modify
If the secondary does not modify the original (e.g., remains silent), Abu Yusuf says the judge asks others; Muhammad says the testimony is rejected because silence implies doubt. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is Abu Yusuf's.
This dispute hinges on whether the secondary's duty includes certification or only transmission.
4
Recognize the conditions that nullify secondary testimony
Secondary testimony is nullified if the original denies having testified, or if the original loses capacity (sinfulness, blindness, apostasy, etc.). Also, if the original says 'we have no testimony' and then dies or disappears, secondary testimony is invalid due to absence of valid transmission (tahmil).
Denial by a present original automatically voids the secondary testimony, even without explicit denial if the original is present? Actually, if present, secondary is disregarded even without denial.
5
Determine the mufta bihi ruling
The operative position for fatwa is Abu Yusuf's view: if the secondary fails to modify, the judge can inquire from other sources. However, it is considered bad practice for a secondary to testify without knowing the original's reliability.
This position balances the need for reliable testimony with practical ease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(فتح، عناية) بإنكار الأصل: [ أي شاهد الأصل الشهادة كقولهم: مالنا شهادة أو لم نشهدهم أو أشهدناهم وغلطنا. (ط)] أو خروجه عن أهليتها بفسق وعمي أو خرس أو ردة أو جنون، ومعنى المسألة أنهم قالوا: مالنا شهادة على هذه الحادثة وماتوا أو غابوا ، ثم جاء الفروع، وشهدوا عند الحاكم بهذه الحادثة لم تقبل شهادتهم؛ لأن التحميل شرط، و لم يوجد، وأما مع حضرتهم فلا يلتفت إلى شهادة الفروع وإن لم ينكروا. [رمز الحقائق: ١٥٨/٢]
And it is valid just as the modification of the secondary witnesses for the originals is valid, so too is the modification of the originals for the secondary witnesses valid. Its summary: that if the judge knows the originals and secondary witnesses by reliability, he judges by their testimony. If he knows one group without the other, he asks about those he does not know. His statement 'valid' means he accepts their modification because they are among the people of modification; for the secondary witness is a deputy transmitting the statement of the original to the judge's court, and by the transmission the rule of deputation ends, so he becomes a third party, thus his modification is valid. The meaning is that the secondary witnesses are known for reliability to the judge, so they modified the originals. If he does not know them for reliability, then they must be modified, and both the originals and secondary must be modified. And just as the modification of the secondary for his original suffices, so too does the modification of one witness for his companion suffice in the most correct view, because a just person is not suspected of like. And if the testimony of a secondary is rejected due to the sinfulness of the original, the testimony of neither of them is accepted thereafter. (Ayni, Fath) 'And otherwise they are modified' means that if the secondary witnesses omit the tazkiya (declaration of reliability) of the originals by remaining silent or saying 'we do not know their state,' the judge asks about the originals from others besides the secondary witnesses. This is the analysis according to Abu Yusuf. Muhammad obligated the secondary witnesses to modify the originals, such that the testimony is not accepted if they do not modify them, because testimony depends on reliability; if they remain silent, they become doubtful about what they testified, so it is not accepted. (Ramz al-Haqaiq 2:158) According to Abu Yusuf, what is taken from them is the transmission of testimony, not the modification of the originals, because modification may be hidden from them. So if they transmit, they have fulfilled what was required of them. Then the judge ascertains reliability just as if the originals had attended themselves and testified, then their testimony is accepted. And if the secondary witness does not know the original's reliability or anything else, he is bad in testifying upon his testimony for abandoning precaution, and the badness is more severe than dislike. (Fath, Inayah) 'By the denial of the original' meaning the original witness denies the testimony, such as they say: 'We have no testimony' or 'We did not witness them' or 'We had them witness but we made a mistake' (T). Or his leaving the capacity for it by sinfulness, blindness, dumbness, apostasy, or insanity. The meaning of the issue is that they say: 'We have no testimony about this incident' and they died or were absent, then the secondary witnesses came and testified before the judge about this incident; their testimony is not accepted because the transmission (tahmil) is a condition and it did not exist. But if they are present, no attention is paid to the testimony of the secondary even if they did not deny. (Ramz al-Haqaiq 2:158)
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage covers three related rules. First, modification (ta'dil): the secondary witnesses may modify the originals, and vice versa, because after transmission the secondary becomes a third party. If the judge knows one group but not the other, he asks about the unknown. According to the most correct view, one witness's modification of his companion suffices. If a secondary's testimony is rejected due to the original's sinfulness, the testimony of neither is accepted later. Second, if the secondary witnesses do not modify the originals (e.g., they remain silent), there is a dispute: Abu Yusuf says the judge asks others about the originals, since the secondary's duty is only transmission; Muhammad says they must modify, otherwise the testimony is rejected because silence indicates doubt. The relied-upon view is that of Abu Yusuf, but he considers it bad practice (is'a') to testify without knowing the original's reliability. Third, nullification (butlan): the secondary's testimony is nullified by the original's denial of the testimony (e.g., saying 'we have no testimony' or 'we made a mistake'), or by the original losing capacity due to sin, blindness, etc. If the originals say they have no testimony and then die or disappear, secondary testimony on that incident is not accepted because the condition of valid transmission (tahmil) is absent. If they are present, even without denial, secondary testimony is disregarded.

Key Terms
تعديل (ta'dil): Declaring a witness to be just and reliable
تزكية (tazkiya): Synonym for ta'dil; purification or certification of reliability
تحميل (tahmil): The act of the original witness transmitting the testimony to the secondary witness

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Secondary testimony is nullified by the original's denial or loss of eligibility; Abu Yusuf's permissive view on modification is the operative Hanafi position.
