Identity Verification in Secondary Testimony and the Judge's Letter
Ruling on identity uncertainty and judge's letter in secondary testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the procedure when identity is uncertain in secondary testimony and explain why a judge's letter is equivalent to two witnesses using the concept of wilaya.

Core Idea
A judge's general authority (wilaya) allows him to stand in place of two witnesses for transmitting testimony.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on what happens when secondary witnesses cannot positively identify the person against whom they testify. It also explores the legal reasoning behind accepting a judge's letter as strong evidence, drawing on the principle of wilaya. The passage presents two practical scenarios and then defends the judge's letter using a rational proof (istihsan).

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that the core problem is uncertainty about the identity of the defendant in secondary testimony scenarios.
2
State the ruling
The claimant must bring two additional witnesses to confirm the identity of the person against whom the testimony is directed.
This applies both when secondary witnesses bring an incorrect person and when they simply cannot recognize the person brought by the claimant.
3
Apply to the judge's letter
Similarly, when a judge's letter is used, and the defendant denies being the person named, the claimant must produce two witnesses to verify identity.
The judge's letter itself is valid evidence but does not override the need for identity confirmation.
4
Understand the objection
Some might object that the judge's letter transmits testimony, which normally requires two witnesses for the transmission itself.
5
Examine the Hanafi response
The judge's general authority (wilaya) and complete justice allow him to stand in place of two persons, analogous to a guardian in contracts.
This is a rational proof (istihsan) based on qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو شهدا على شهادة رجلين على فلانة بنت فلان الفلانية بألف وقالا أخبرانا أنهما يعرفانها، فجاء الشاهدان الفرعان بامرأة، وقالا: لم ندر أهي هذه أم لا قيل للمدعي هات شاهدين أنها فلانة، وكذا لو شهدا على شهادة رجلين على فلانة بنت فلان الفلانية المذكورة بألف، وقالا أخبرانا أنهما يعرفانها، فجاء المدعي بامرأة، وقال الشاهدان الفرعان لم نعلم الفلانية أي التي جاء بها المدعي، قيل للمدعي هات شاهدين آخرين يشهدان أن هذه المرأة هي الفلانية المذكورة. (عيني) كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي إلخ : أي إذا كتب القاضي إلى القاضي الآخر أن فلاناً وفلاناً شهدا عندي بكذا من المال للمدعي على فلانة بنت فلان الفلانية، وأحضر المدعي امرأة عند القاضي المكتوب إليه، وأنكرت المرأة أن تكون هي المنسوبة بتلك النسبة المذكورة في الكتاب، فلابد من شاهدين آخرين يشهدان أن هذه المرأة هي المنسوبة بتلك النسبة، كما في المسألة الأولى [ رمز الحقائق: ١٥٩/٢] فإن قيل: إن كتاب القاضي نقل شهادة الأصول في الحقيقة ولابد لنقل الشهادة من الشاهدين للولاية، قلنا: إن القاضي لعموم ولايته وكمال عدالته قائم مقام الاثنين، وللولاية تأثير في تنزيل شخص مقام الشخصين كولي طرفي العقد.
And if they testify upon the testimony of two men against so-and-so daughter of so-and-so the such-and-such for one thousand, and they said: 'They informed us that they know her,' then the two secondary witnesses brought a woman and said: 'We do not know if she is this one or not,' it is said to the claimant: 'Bring two witnesses that she is so-and-so.' Similarly, if they testify upon the testimony of two men against so-and-so daughter of so-and-so the aforementioned such-and-such for one thousand, and they said: 'They informed us that they know her,' then the claimant brought a woman, and the two secondary witnesses said: 'We do not know the such-and-such, i.e., the one the claimant brought,' it is said to the claimant: 'Bring two other witnesses that this woman is the aforementioned such-and-such.' (Ayni) 'The judge's letter to the judge etc.' means: if the judge writes to another judge that so-and-so and so-and-so testified before me for such-and-such property for the claimant against so-and-so daughter of so-and-so the such-and-such, and the claimant brings a woman before the judge to whom it is written, and the woman denies that she is the one described with that description mentioned in the letter, then it is necessary to have two other witnesses that this woman is the one described with that description, as in the first issue. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 2:159] If it is said: 'The judge's letter actually transmits the testimony of the originals, and the transmission of testimony requires two witnesses for authority,' we say: 'The judge, due to his general authority and complete justice, stands in the place of two, and authority has the effect of placing one person in the place of two, like the guardian of the two contracting parties.'
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage addresses cases where the identity of the person against whom testimony is given is uncertain. In the first scenario, secondary witnesses testify based on information from two original witnesses that they know a specific woman, but when they see a woman brought by the claimant, they are unsure if she is the same person. The claimant must bring two witnesses to confirm identity. The same applies if the secondary witnesses do not recognize the woman the claimant brings. This rule is analogous to the case of a judge's letter. When a judge writes to another judge transferring testimony, and the defendant denies being the person named in the letter, the claimant must bring two witnesses to verify her identity. The passage then defends the legal validity of one judge writing a letter as equivalent to two witnesses, because the judge's general authority and complete justice allow him to stand in place of two persons, similar to how a guardian can act for both contracting parties. This ruling ensures that rights are established despite the difficulty of transmitting testimony.

Key Terms
ولاية (wilaya): Legal authority of the judge to act in place of two witnesses
شهادة على شهادة (shahada ala shahada): Secondary testimony; testimony based on the testimony of others
كتاب القاضي (kitab al-qadi): Judge's letter; a written communication from one judge to another transmitting testimony

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a judge's letter is sent to another judge, why is it considered equivalent to two witnesses?
A) Because the judge is always trusted.
B) Because of his general authority and complete justice.
C) Because it is written down.
D) Because two judges are needed for testimony.

Key Takeaway
When identity is uncertain in secondary testimony, two additional witnesses must confirm identity; and a judge's letter is valid evidence due to the judge's authority (wilaya).

Conditions for Secondary Testimony: Nullification, Identification, and the Tazkiyah Dispute
Explains nullification and identification rules for secondary testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for valid secondary testimony and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether secondary witnesses must attest to the integrity of primary witnesses.

Core Idea
Secondary testimony is valid only if primary witnesses do not deny and identification is precise; the tazkiyah requirement is disputed within the school.

This lesson examines the rules of secondary testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada) as set forth in Kanz al-Daqaiq. We will explore when such testimony is nullified, how identification must be specified, and the key difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan on whether secondary witnesses must verify the integrity of the primary witnesses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Secondary testimony is permissible under conditions. The passage first states that it is nullified if primary witnesses deny or become disqualified. Also, secondary witnesses must declare the primary witnesses upright (or else the testimony is nullified).
The phrase 'وإلا عُدّلوا' indicates a requirement to affirm integrity, but this is disputed.
2
Apply the nullification rules
If the primary witness (asl) denies having testified or becomes disqualified (e.g., fasiq, blind), the secondary testimony (far') is automatically invalid. This is a key condition for validity.
Denial includes both denial of testimony and denial of the underlying event.
3
Analyze the identification requirement
When secondary witnesses are uncertain about the identity of the person they testified about, the plaintiff must bring two witnesses to establish her identity. Similarly, if the description is too general (e.g., 'Tamimi'), it is insufficient until the sub-tribe is specified.
This applies both to direct secondary testimony and to testimony via a judge's letter.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
The passage implies a dispute: Abu Yusuf holds that secondary witnesses need not attest to the integrity of the primary witnesses; the judge can verify. Muhammad holds that they must, because testimony depends on integrity.
The dispute is about the requirement to expressly declare (ta'dil) the primary witnesses' uprightness.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If secondary witnesses do not mention integrity, Abu Yusuf accepts their testimony; Muhammad rejects it unless they affirm integrity. The practical consequence affects the burden of proof on the plaintiff.
The mufta bihi is not explicitly stated in this passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الشهادة على الشهادة
وإلا عُدّلوا، وتبطل شهادة الفرع بإنكار الأصل الشهادة، ولو شهدا على شهادة رجلين على فلانة بنت فلان الفلانية بألف وقالا أخبرانا أنهما يعرفانها، فجاء بامرأة، وقالا: لم ندر أهي هذه أم لا قيل للمدعي هات شاهدين أنها فلانة، وكذا كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي، ولو قالا فيهما: التميمية، لم تجز حتى ينسباها إلى فخذها.
أي وإن لم يعدلهم الفروع... (طويل، لكن الأهم: ذكر الخلاف بين أبي يوسف ومحمد في تعديل الفروع للأصول، وأنكر الأصل الشهادة، والخروج عن الأهلية، والتعريف بالنسب).
Chapter of Testimony upon Testimony
And if they do not declare them upright, the testimony of the branch is nullified by the denial of the original witness.
And if two witnesses testify upon the testimony of two men against a certain woman, daughter of so-and-so, the such-and-such, for a thousand, and they say: 'They informed us that they know her', then he brings a woman, and they say: 'We do not know if this is her or not', it is said to the plaintiff: 'Bring two witnesses that she is that woman'. And similarly if the judge writes to another judge.
And if they say in both: 'the Tamimi', it is not permissible until they attribute her to her sub-tribe.
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq deals with the conditions for valid secondary testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada). The first ruling: secondary testimony is nullified if the primary witness denies having testified or becomes disqualified (by fisq, blindness, etc.). The second ruling: if secondary witnesses cannot identify the person with certainty, the plaintiff must bring two witnesses to establish identity. This applies whether the testimony is direct or via a judge's letter. The third ruling: if the identification is too general (e.g., 'Tamimi'), it is insufficient; the witnesses must specify the sub-tribe. The commentary includes an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf holds that secondary witnesses need not attest to the integrity of the primary witnesses; the judge can verify. Muhammad holds they must, because testimony depends on integrity. The Hanafi position is that the secondary witnesses' duty is only to transmit testimony; integrity may be hidden from them.

Key Terms
شهادة الفرع (shahadat al-far'): Secondary testimony, i.e., testimony given based on the testimony of primary witnesses.
إنكار الأصل (inkar al-asl): Denial by the primary witness that he gave testimony or that he witnessed the event.
تزكية (tazkiyah): Attesting to the integrity ('adalah) of a witness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The judge must decide based on his own knowledge.
C) The plaintiff must bring two witnesses that she is that specific woman.
D) The secondary witnesses must be punished.

Key Takeaway
Secondary testimony requires precise identification and is nullified by the primary witness's denial or disqualification; the school differs on whether secondary witnesses must also attest to the primary witnesses' integrity.

Punishment for Perjury: Ta'zir through Tashhir
States the Hanafi ruling on punishment for perjury and the disagreement with the two companions and Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ta'zir for perjury, identify the conditions that trigger it, and explain the difference between Abu Hanifa's position and that of the Sahibayn and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Perjury requires ta'zir by consensus, but Abu Hanifa limits it to public exposure; no beating or imprisonment.

In this passage, we examine the punishment for perjury (shahadat al-zur), a crime that undermines the integrity of the judiciary. While all scholars agree that a false witness must be punished, they differ sharply on the method. Abu Hanifa argues for public humiliation through tashhir, following the practice of the Tabi'i judge Shuraih. Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i insist on beating and imprisonment, citing the precedent of Caliph 'Umar. Understanding this dispute teaches us how Hanafi fiqh prioritizes the practice of the early community over individual reports.

Guided Path
1
Identify when ta'zir is imposed
The passage states that ta'zir applies only when the witness admits to intentional false testimony. If they claim mistake, forgetfulness, or if their testimony was rejected for procedural reasons, no ta'zir is given.
This threshold is crucial: the witness must confess to deliberate lying.
2
Recognize the consensus on wajib ta'zir
All scholars agree that ta'zir for perjury is wajib, whether or not judgment was passed. The dispute is about the form, not the obligation.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the punishment is tashhir (public exposure only) – parading the perjurer in his marketplace or among his people after 'Asr, announcing him as a false witness, without beating or blackening his face.
This is derived from the practice of Shuraih, a Tabi'i judge.
4
State the opposing view
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) along with al-Shafi'i hold that the perjurer should be beaten (forty lashes following 'Umar's precedent) and imprisoned.
This is based on an action attributed to 'Umar ibn al-Khattab.
5
Analyze the Hanafi evidence
The Hanafi response is that Shuraih's practice (tashhir only) was known to the Companions, who did not object, indicating it is Sunnah. 'Umar's action is seen as a specific case, not a general rule.
This shows how Hanafi usul prioritizes consistent practice over isolated reports.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أقر إلخ: أي أقر أنه شهد زوراً أو كاذباً متعمداً، وأما إذا قال: غلطت أو نسيت أو أخطأت، أو ردت شهادته لتهمة أو لمخالفة بين الدعوى والشهادة، فإنه لا يعزر والرجال والنساء وأهل الذمة في شهادة الزور سواء، وقوله: "يشهر" ضبط بعضهم بضم الياء وسكون الشين من الإفعال وضبطه بعضهم بتشديد الهاء من التفعيل. واعلم أن شاهد الزور يعزر إجماعاً، اتصل القضاء بشهادته أو لم يتصل واختلفوا في التعزير، فقال أبو حنيفة: تغريره تشهيره، ولا يضرب، ولا يسود وجهه، فيبعثه إلى سوقه إن كان سوقياً أو إلى قومه إن كان غير سوقي بعد العصر في أجمع ما كانوا مع أعوانه أعم من أن يكون ماشياً أو راكباً، ويقول: إنا وجدنا هذا شاهد زور فاحذروه، وحذروا الناس منه، وقالا : يضرب ويحبس وهو قول الشافعي؛ لأن عمر [؟] ضرب شاهد الزور أربعين وسود وجهه وله أن شريحاً كان يشهره، ولا يضربه، وهو وإن كان تابعياً لكن زاحم الصحابة في الفتوى، وكان قاضياً معروفاً بالعدل في زمن عمر عليه السلام، والصحابة متوافرة ما كان يخفي عليهم ما يعمله، سوطاً،
And if he confesses etc.: i.e., he confesses that he testified falsely or intentionally lying. But if he says: 'I was mistaken or I forgot or I erred', or his testimony was rejected due to suspicion or conflict between claim and testimony, then he is not punished. Men, women, and dhimmis are equal in perjury. And the word 'yushahhir' (he is exposed) is pronounced by some with a damma on the ya' and sukun on the shin (from if'al) and by some with tashdid of the ha' (from taf'il). Know that the perjurer is punished by ta'zir by consensus, whether judgment was passed based on his testimony or not. They differed on the ta'zir: Abu Hanifa said his ignominy is his exposure; he is not beaten, nor is his face blackened. He is sent to his market if he is a market-person, or to his people if not, after 'asr, in the most crowded place, with his assistants, whether walking or riding, and it is said: 'We have found this one to be a false witness, so beware of him,' and the people are warned against him. The two said: He is beaten and imprisoned, and this is the view of al-Shafi'i, because 'Umar [؟] beat a false witness forty lashes and blackened his face. And it is reported that Shuraih used to expose him and not beat him, and although he was a Tabi'i, he competed with the Companions in giving fatwa, and was a judge known for justice in the time of 'Umar (peace be upon him), and the Companions were numerous and what he did was not hidden from them. A whip!
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage addresses the punishment for perjury (shahadat al-zur). The first point: if a witness admits to intentional false testimony, he is subject to ta'zir. But if he claims mistake, forgetfulness, or if his testimony was rejected for other reasons, no ta'zir is imposed. All are equal in this. The central dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that the punishment is public exposure (tashhir) only – parading the perjurer in his market or community after 'asr, announcing him as a false witness, without beating or blackening his face. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (along with al-Shafi'i) hold that he should be beaten (forty lashes following 'Umar's precedent) and imprisoned. The Hanafi argument relies on the practice of Shuraih, a Tabi'i judge, who only exposed and did not beat, and whose practice was not rejected by the Companions. This indicates that tashhir is the established sunnah, while 'Umar's action was a specific instance that may have been for additional deterrence.

Key Terms
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for offenses without fixed hadd penalty; for perjury, it is wajib.
تغرير (taghrir): Ignominy or humiliation as punishment; Abu Hanifa equates it with tashhir.
تشهير (tashhir): Public exposure of the culprit, parading him, and announcing his crime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Imprisonment for one year.
C) Public exposure (tashhir) in the market or among his people.
D) A fine and warning.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school mandates ta'zir for perjury through public exposure only, distinguishing it from the view of the Sahibayn and al-Shafi'i who add beating and imprisonment.

Requirement to Specify Sub-Tribe in Testimony
Ruling on testimony given with general tribal affiliation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that testimony using only a general tribal name is invalid, define the term fakhdh as the required level of specificity, and apply the principle that identification must remove ambiguity.

Core Idea
A general tribal name is legally insufficient — you must specify the sub-tribe (fakhdh) to remove ambiguity.

This passage tackles a practical problem: when a witness identifies a person only by a large tribal affiliation, the testimony is not accepted because many individuals share that name. The Hanafi school requires specifying the sub-tribe (fakhdh) — the narrowest genealogical division — to achieve certain identification. The commentary also explains the full hierarchy of Arab genealogical terms, from the broadest (sha'b) to the most specific (fakhdh).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problematic Testimony
Consider the case where witnesses say 'al-Tamimiyyah' (the Tamimi woman). This is the scenario the passage examines. Identify why this is problematic: the tribe Banu Tamim is so large that many women share the same name and father's name.
2
Grasp the Necessity of Certain Identification
Understand that the purpose of testimony is to establish a fact about a specific individual. If the identification is ambiguous, the testimony fails to achieve its goal. The passage states 'knowledge of her identity is not attained' without specifying the sub-tribe.
3
Distinguish General vs Specific Lineage
Learn the genealogical hierarchy: sha'b (nation) → qabilah (tribe) → fasilah (sept) → 'imarah (sub-tribe) → batn (clan) → fakhdh (sub-clan). The passage gives examples (Khuzaymah, Kinanah, etc.) to illustrate. fakhdh is the most specific level, equivalent to naming the highest grandfather.
Memorize the order: sha'b, qabilah, fasilah, 'imarah, batn, fakhdh (with fakhdh being the most specific).
4
Apply the Principle to the Ruling
The ruling is that testimony with only a general tribal name is not permissible. The witnesses must trace the person to her fakhdh (sub-tribe). This fulfills the requirement of ta'rīf (identification) that removes ambiguity.
5
Consider Exceptions and Nuances
The passage notes that for a present person, pointing suffices. For an absent person famous by name (like Abu Hanifah), the name alone is enough. For an unknown person, name and father suffice if accompanied by profession or sub-tribe, but there is a difference of opinion about whether the grandfather must be mentioned. The criterion is always: does this identify the person with certainty?
The principle: 'the goal of lineage is to attain knowledge of the person'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قالا فيهما: التميمية، لم تجز حتى ينسباها إلى فخذها. التميمية: أي فلانة بنت فلان التميمية لم تجز: لأن بني تميم قوم لا يحصون، فتكون بينهم المتحدات أساميهن وأسامي آبائهن فلا يحصل العلم بالنسبة إليه، بل يحصل العلم بالنسبة إلى الفخذ، كما أشار إليه بقوله: "حتى ينسباها إلى فخذها". ينسباها إلى فخذها هو القبيلة الخاصة أي الجد الأعلى أو جدها؛ إذ لابد من التعريف، وهو لا يحصل بالنسبة العامة والنسبة إلى بني تميم عامة؛ إذ لا يحصى عددهم بخلاف النسبة إلى الفخذ؛ لأنها خاصة حتى إن ذكره يقوم مقام ذكر الجد؛ لأنه اسم الجد الأعلى، فقام مقام ذكر الجد الأدنى، وهو أب الأب. والفخذ: بالكسر وبالسكون للتخفيف دون القبيلة، وقيل: دون البطن؛ لأن أول النسب الشعب بالفتح، ثم القبيلة ثم الفصيلة ثم العمارة ثم البطن ثم الفخذ فكان أخص من الكل، وجعل الزمخشري الفصيلة آخر الكل، فالشعب مجمع القبائل، والقبيلة مجمع الفصائل والفصيلة مجمع العمائر، والعمارة مجمع البطون، والبطن مجمع الأفخاذ. مثلا: خزيمة شعب، وكنانة قبيلة وقريش عمارة وقصي بطن وهاشم فخذ، والمقصود من النسب حصول العلم بالمنسوب، فلو ذكر اسمه واسم أبيه وفخذه أو صناعته، ولم يذكر الجد يقبل، وشرط الأستروشني للتعريف ذكر ثلاثة أشياء، وفي اشتراط ذكر الجد اختلاف والحاصل أن التعريف بالإشارة إلى الحاضر، وفي الغائب إن كان معروفاً بالاسم المجرد مشهوراً كأبي حنيفة، يكفي، ولا حاجة إلى ذكر الأب والجد، فالمعتبر إنما هو حصول المعرفة وارتفاع الاشتراك.
And if both witnesses say in them: 'the Tamimi woman', it is not permissible until they trace her to her sub-tribe. 'the Tamimi woman': i.e., so-and-so daughter of so-and-so al-Tamimiyya. It is not permissible because Banu Tamim are a people whose numbers cannot be counted, so among them there may be those whose names and fathers' names are identical; thus knowledge of her identity is not attained, rather knowledge is attained only by specifying the sub-tribe, as he indicated by his statement: 'until they trace her to her sub-tribe'. 'Trace her to her sub-tribe': it is the specific tribe, i.e., the highest grandfather or her grandfather; because definition is necessary, and it is not achieved by general lineage, and the lineage to Banu Tamim is general, since their numbers cannot be counted, unlike the lineage to the sub-tribe, because it is specific, even that its mention stands in place of the mention of the grandfather; because it is the name of the highest grandfather, so it stands in place of the mention of the lower grandfather, who is the father's father. And al-fakhdh: with a kasrah and with sukoon for ease of pronunciation, it is below the qabilah (tribe), and it is said: below the batn (clan); because the first level of lineage is al-sha'b (nation) with fathah, then al-qabilah, then al-fasilah (sept), then al-‘imarah (sub-tribe), then al-batn (clan), then al-fakhdh, so it is the most specific of all. Al-Zamakhshari considered al-fasilah as the last of all. So al-sha'b is the grouping of tribes; al-qabilah is the grouping of septs; al-fasilah is the grouping of sub-tribes; al-‘imarah is the grouping of clans; al-batn is the grouping of sub-tribes. For example: Khuzaymah is a sha'b, Kinanah is a qabilah, Quraysh is an 'imarah, Qusayy is a batn, and Hashim is a fakhdh. And the goal of lineage is to attain knowledge of the person. So if he mentions his name, his father's name, and his sub-tribe or his profession, and does not mention the grandfather, it is accepted. Al-Ustruwshani stipulated for definition the mention of three things, and there is difference regarding the stipulation of mentioning the grandfather. The conclusion is that definition by pointing is for the present, and for the absent, if he is well-known by the bare name, famous like Abu Hanifah, it suffices, and there is no need to mention the father and grandfather. So the criterion is only the attainment of knowledge and the removal of ambiguity.
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling concerning the requirement of precise identification in testimony (shahadah). The text addresses a specific case: when witnesses testify about a woman and identify her only by a general tribal affiliation (e.g., 'the Tamimi woman'), the testimony is not accepted because the tribe of Tamim is so large that many women share the same name and father's name. The necessary knowledge of identity is not achieved. Therefore, the witnesses must specify her sub-tribe (fakhdh), which is a more specific genealogical division (e.g., the clan of Hashim). The commentary explains the hierarchy of genealogical terms: sha'b (nation), qabilah (tribe), fasilah (sept), 'imarah (sub-tribe), batn (clan), and fakhdh (sub-clan). The principle is that identification must remove all ambiguity. For a present person, pointing suffices. For an absent person, if he is famously known (like Abu Hanifah), his name alone is enough; otherwise, additional details such as father, grandfather, or sub-tribe may be required. The key is to achieve certainty and avoid confusion.

Key Terms
تميمية (Tamīmiyyah): A woman belonging to the large tribe of Banu Tamim; used as an example of inadequate identification in testimony.
فخذ (fakhdh): The specific sub-tribe or clan, the narrowest genealogical division below batn.
تعريف (ta'rīf): The process of legally identifying a person so that there is no ambiguity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Punishment of a False Witness Who Confesses: Ta'zeer and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on punishing a false witness who confesses, with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ta'zeer for a false witness who confesses, explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and identify when his future testimony is accepted.

Core Idea
A false witness who confesses intentionally is punished by tashhir (public exposure), not beating—this is the mufta bihi view of Imam Abu Hanifa.

This passage addresses the punishment of a witness who admits to giving false testimony. While all scholars agree that such a witness is subject to ta'zeer (discretionary punishment), there is a significant disagreement within the Hanafi school itself. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that merely making him known to the public (tashhir) is sufficient, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, along with Imam al-Shafi'i, argue for beating and imprisonment. The passage also discusses the conditions under which a repentant false witness may have his future testimony accepted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its consensus ruling
Recognize that false testimony (shahadat al-zur) is a major sin (haram) and there is consensus (ijma') that the witness is subject to ta'zeer, regardless of whether his testimony was acted upon.
The consensus applies to the discretionary punishment, not its specific form.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the punishment is tashhir: the witness is paraded to his market or tribe after 'Asr, and people are warned against him. No beating, no blackening of face, no imprisonment.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, along with al-Shafi'i, hold that the false witness must be beaten and imprisoned. Their proof is the action of Umar ibn al-Khattab who beat a false witness forty lashes.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Analyze the proofs
Abu Hanifa's proof comes from the practice of Shuraih, a Tabi'i judge who only made the witness known, and the silence of the Companions. The Hanafi response to Umar's action is that it was a political measure (siyasah) because the number of lashes reached the hadd of a slave for qadhf.
The principle: ta'zeer should not exceed the nearest hadd.
5
Apply the tarjih
The text explicitly states that the fatwa is on the Imam's (Abu Hanifa's) statement. Therefore, the operative ruling is tashhir only.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(فتح، شلبي) ولو أقر إلخ: أي أقر أنه شهد زوراً أو كاذباً متعمداً، وأما إذا قال: غلطت أو نسيت أو أخطأت، أو ردت شهادته لتهمة أو لمخالفة بين الدعوى والشهادة، فإنه لا يعزر والرجال والنساء وأهل الذمة في شهادة الزور سواء، وقوله: "يشهر" ضبط بعضهم بضم الياء وسكون الشين من الإفعال وضبطه بعضهم بتشديد الهاء من التفعيل. واعلم أن شاهد الزور يعزر إجماعاً، اتصل القضاء بشهادته أو لم يتصل واختلفوا في التعزير، فقال أبو حنيفة: تغريره تشهيره، ولا يضرب، ولا يسود وجهه، فيبعثه إلى سوقه إن كان سوقياً أو إلى قومه إن كان غير سوقي بعد العصر في أجمع ما كانوا مع أعوانه أعم من أن يكون ماشياً أو راكباً، ويقول: إنا وجدنا هذا شاهد زور فاحذروه، وحذروا الناس منه، وقالا : يضرب ويحبس وهو قول الشافعي؛ لأن عمر ضرب شاهد الزور أربعين وسود وجهه وله أن شريحاً كان يشهره، ولا يضربه، وهو وإن كان تابعياً لكن زاحم الصحابة في الفتوى، وكان قاضياً معروفاً بالعدل في زمن عمر والصحابة متوافرة ما كان يخفي عليهم ما يعمله، وسكتوا عنه، فكان كالمروي عنهم، وحل محل الإجماع، ولأن الانزجار يحصل بالتشهير، فيكتفي به، وما ورد عن عمر محمول على السياسة بدلالة تبليغ التعزير إلى أربعين وهو حد العبد في القذف. وقال الإمام الحاكم أبو محمد الكاتب : هذه المسألة على ثلاثة أوجه أحدها: أن يرجع على سبيل التوبة والندامة، فإنه لا يعزر بالإجماع، والثاني: أن يرجع من غير التوبة، وهو مُصرّ على ما كان، فإنه يعزر بالضرب بالإجماع، والثالث: أن لا يعلم رجوعه بأي سبب كان بأن لا يعلم أنه يتوب عن شهادة الزور أو بغيره من العصيان، فإنه على الاختلاف المذكور، والفتوى على قول الإمام وهل تقبل شهادته بعد ذلك إذا تاب؟ قالوا: إذا كان فاسقا تقبل؛ لأن الذي حمله على الشهادة الباطلة فسقه فإذا تاب ظهر صلاحه، فتقبل؛ لزوال الفسق. واختلفوا في مقدار مدة التوبة، فقدره بعضهم بستة أشهر، وبعضهم بسنة، وكذا في مدة الحبس، والصحيح: أنه مفوض إلى رأي القاضي، وإن كان عدلاً أو مستوراً لا تقبل شهادته أبداً؛ لأنه لا يعتمد على عدالته، ولأن الحامل له على ذلك غير معلوم، فكان الحال قبل التوبة وبعدها سواء، وعن أبي يوسف: أن شهادته تقبل، وبه يفتى، قيل: إنما وضع المسألة في الإقرار ؛ لأنه لا طريق إلى بيان معرفة ذلك بالبينة، لكن ذكر في "المغني": أن شهادة الزور قد تعلم بدون الإقرار كما يشهد بموت رجل أو بقتله، فيجيء المشهود بالموت، أو القتل حياً، هذا أن شهادة الزور قد تكون بدون الإقرار بالكذب، لكن لا ينبغي أن يختص التعزير بالإقرار بذلك متعمداً. (عيني، فتح، عناية)
And if the two original witnesses confess this testimony, i.e., the two original witnesses. And the implication of restricting the issue to the denial of the woman is that if she were not denying, the plaintiff would not be required to bring two other witnesses to testify to that present lineage, contrary to what is in 'al-Bahr' that he is required even if she affirms, due to the possibility of forgery. (Fath, Shalabi). 'And if he confesses, etc.': i.e., he confesses that he gave false testimony or lied intentionally. But if he says: I made a mistake, or forgot, or erred, or his testimony was rejected due to suspicion or discrepancy between the claim and testimony, then he is not punished. Men, women, and dhimmis are equal in false testimony. His statement 'he is made known' (yushahhar) – some scholars read it with dammah on the ya and sukun on the shin from af'ala, and some read it with shaddah on the ha from taf'eel. Know that the false witness is disciplined (yu'azzar) by consensus, whether his testimony was acted upon or not. They differed about the punishment: Abu Hanifa said: his penalty is to be made known (tashhir), and he is not beaten, nor is his face blackened. He is sent to his market if he is a market-person, or to his people if he is not a market-person, after 'Asr in the most crowded place with his assistants, whether walking or riding, and they say: 'Indeed we found this person a false witness, beware of him, and warn people against him.' And both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he is beaten and imprisoned, and this is the opinion of al-Shafi'i, because Umar beat a false witness forty lashes and blackened his face. And (Abu Hanifa) argued that Shuraih used to make him known and not beat him. And although Shuraih was a Tabi'i, he competed with the Companions in fatwa, and was a judge known for justice in the time of Umar, and the Companions were abundant, and what he did was not hidden from them, and they remained silent about it, so it was like a narration from them and took the place of consensus. Because deterrence is achieved by making known, so it suffices. And what is reported from Umar is interpreted as being for political reasons (siyasah), indicated by the fact that the punishment reached forty lashes, which is the hadd of a slave for slander. Imam al-Hakim Abu Muhammad al-Katib said: This issue is on three aspects: one: he retracts by way of repentance and remorse – then he is not punished by consensus. Second: he retracts without repentance, persisting in his falsehood – then he is punished by beating by consensus. Third: his retraction is not known for any reason, i.e., it is not known whether he repented from false testimony or from other disobedience – then there is the difference mentioned. The fatwa is on the Imam's (Abu Hanifa's) statement. And if he repents thereafter, is his testimony accepted? They said: if he was a fasiq, it is accepted, because what drove him to false testimony was his fisq; when he repents his rightousness appears, so it is accepted due to the removal of fisq. They differed about the duration of repentance: some estimated six months, some a year. Similarly for the duration of imprisonment. The correct view is that it is left to the judge's discretion. If he was righteous ('adl) or of unknown status (mastur), his testimony is never accepted, because his trustworthiness is not relied upon, and the motive for his action is unknown, so his state before and after repentance is the same. From Abu Yusuf: his testimony is accepted, and this is what is given fatwa. It is said that the issue is placed in confession because there is no way to know it through evidence. However, in 'al-Mughni' it is mentioned that false testimony may be known without confession, as when someone testifies to a man's death or murder, and the person who was testified to appear alive. So false testimony may be without confessing to lying. But it is not appropriate to restrict punishment to confession of that intentionally. (Ayni, Fath, Inayah)
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed ruling on the punishment (ta'zeer) of a witness who confesses to having given false testimony (shahadat al-zur). It falls under the chapter of testimony on testimony (shahadah 'ala al-shahadah) but deals with the original witnesses admitting falsehood. The passage begins by noting that the issue is usually framed when the woman (the party against whom testimony was given) denies; if she does not deny, the plaintiff is not required to bring new witnesses, though al-Bahr holds otherwise. The core of this passage is the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that the false witness should be 'made known' (tashhir) by being paraded and publicly announced as a liar, without beating or blackening the face. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that he should be beaten and imprisoned, which agrees with al-Shafi'i. Abu Hanifa's proof relies on the practice of Shuraih (a Tabi'i judge) who only made known and did not beat, and the Companions' silence implying approval. Umar's beating of a false witness is considered a political measure. The passage then categorizes three scenarios according to al-Hakim: (1) retraction with repentance – no punishment (consensus); (2) retraction without repentance – beating (consensus); (3) unknown retraction – the difference remains. The fatwa is on Abu Hanifa's view. After repentance, the witness's future testimony is accepted if he was a fasiq (sinner), since his fisq is removed; but if he was 'adl (righteous) or mastur (unknown), his testimony is never accepted. A different narration from Abu Yusuf accepts it. False testimony can also be known without confession, e.g., if the alleged deceased appears alive.

Key Terms
شاهد زور (shāhid zūr): A witness who intentionally gives false testimony.
تعزير (ta'zīr): Discretionary punishment for sins that have no fixed hadd; used for false testimony.
تشهير (tashhīr): Publicly announcing the person's crime to warn people, without physical punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon fatwa in the text, what is the punishment for a false witness who confesses intentionally, without evidence of repentance?
A) Beating of forty lashes
B) Imprisonment for one year
C) Tashhir (public exposure)
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position punishes a false witness who confesses by public exposure (tashhir), not physical beating, based on the practice of Shuraih and the principle that ta'zeer should be minimal for deterrence.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
The Punishment of a False Witness: Shaming over Beating
Punishment rules for false witness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the punishment of a false witness and explain the three-case classification that determines when ta'zir is applied.

Core Idea
A false witness is publicly shamed, not beaten — unless he persists without repentance.

In Hanafi fiqh, false testimony is punished by ta'zir, but the preferred form is shaming rather than beating. This lesson explores the ruling, its evidence, and the three scenarios outlined by Imam al-Katib that dictate when ta'zir is applied.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary punishment
The text begins by stating that a false witness is 'shamed and not given ta'zir' (lashes). Understand that 'ta'zir' here specifically refers to beating.
Shaming (tashhir) is itself a form of ta'zir.
2
Analyze the three-case classification
The false witness is divided into three cases: (1) retracts with repentance → no ta'zir by consensus; (2) retracts without repentance → ta'zir by beating by consensus; (3) retraction unknown → disagreement exists, with fatwa on Abu Hanifa's view (i.e., ta'zir is applied).
Case 3 is the subject of intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Understand the evidentiary basis
Shaming suffices for deterrence; the narration from 'Umar (forty lashes) is interpreted as siyasa (policy), not a fixed hadd.
The maximum ta'zir is set at forty lashes, analogous to the hadd of a slave in qadhf.
4
Apply the classification
Given a specific scenario (e.g., a witness testifies falsely, then repents openly), determine which case applies and the appropriate punishment.
Use the three-case framework as the decision tree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادة أنه شهد زوراً، يشهر ولا يعزر. الشاهد في السوق أو في محلته بالضرب والحبس. باب الشهادة على الشهادة وسكتوا عنه، فكان كالمروي عنهم، وحل محل الإجماع، ولأن الانزجار يحصل بالتشهير، فيكتفي به، وما ورد عن عمر له محمول على السياسة بدلالة تبليغ التعزير إلى أربعين وهو حد العبد في القذف. وقال الإمام الحاكم أبو محمد الكاتب : هذه المسألة على ثلاثة أوجه أحدها: أن يرجع على سبيل التوبة والندامة، فإنه لا يعزر بالإجماع، والثاني: أن يرجع من غير التوبة، وهو مُصرّ على ما كان، فإنه يعزر بالضرب بالإجماع، والثالث: أن لا يعلم رجوعه بأي سبب كان بأن لا يعلم أنه يتوب عن شهادة الزور أو بغيره من العصيان، فإنه على الاختلاف المذكور، والفتوى على قول الإمام وهل تقبل شهادته بعد ذلك إذا تاب؟ قالوا: إذا كان فاسقا تقبل؛ لأن الذي حمله على الشهادة الباطلة فسقه فإذا تاب ظهر صلاحه، فتقبل؛ لزوال الفسق. واختلفوا في مقدار مدة التوبة، فقدره بعضهم بستة أشهر، وبعضهم بسنة، وكذا في مدة الحبس، والصحيح: أنه مفوض إلى رأي القاضي، وإن كان عدلاً أو مستوراً لا تقبل شهادته أبداً؛ لأنه لا يعتمد على عدالته، ولأن الحامل له على ذلك غير معلوم، فكان الحال قبل التوبة وبعدها سواء، وعن أبي يوسف: أن شهادته تقبل، وبه يفتى، قيل: إنما وضع المسألة في الإقرار؛ لأنه لا طريق إلى بيان معرفة ذلك بالبينة، لكن ذكر في "المغني": أن شهادة الزور قد تعلم بدون الإقرار كما يشهد بموت رجل أو بقتله، فيجيء المشهود بالموت أو القتل حياً، هذا أن شهادة الزور قد تكون بدون الإقرار بالكذب، لكن لا ينبغي أن يختص التعزير بالإقرار بذلك فعلل من متعمداً. (عيني، فتح، عناية)
The Book of Testimony: That he testified falsely, he is publicly shamed and not punished with ta'zir (lashes). The witness in the market or in his neighborhood with beating and imprisonment. Chapter of Testimony upon Testimony: And they remained silent about it, so it was like what is reported from them, and it took the place of consensus, and because deterrence is achieved by public shaming, so it suffices, and what is reported from 'Umar is interpreted as policy (siyasa) indicated by the extent of ta'zir reaching forty, which is the hadd of a slave in qadhf. Al-Hakim Abu Muhammad al-Katib said: This issue has three aspects: First, that he retracts with repentance and regret, then he is not punished with ta'zir by consensus. Second, that he retracts without repentance, while persisting in what he did, then he is punished with beating by consensus. Third, that his retraction is not known by any means, i.e., it is not known whether he repents from false testimony or from other disobedience, then it is according to the mentioned disagreement, and the fatwa is on the statement of the Imam. And is his testimony accepted after that if he repents? They said: If he was a sinner (fasiq), it is accepted, because what drove him to false testimony was his sinfulness; so if he repents, his integrity becomes apparent, so it is accepted due to the removal of sinfulness. They differed on the duration of repentance, some estimated it as six months, some as a year, and likewise for imprisonment, and the correct opinion is that it is left to the judge's discretion. And if he was just or of unknown status, his testimony is never accepted, because his integrity is not relied upon, and because the cause for him [to testify falsely] is unknown, so the situation before and after repentance is the same. From Abu Yusuf: His testimony is accepted, and according to this fatwa is given. It was said: The issue is placed in confession (iqrar), because there is no way to know that by evidence, but it is mentioned in al-Mughni that false testimony may be known without confession, as when one testifies to a man's death or killing, then the one testified as dead or killed comes alive. This shows that false testimony may be without confession of lying, but ta'zir should not be restricted to confession in that [case] deliberately. (Ayni, Fath, Inaya)
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq deals with the ruling on a false witness (shahid zoor). The passage type is a ruling statement with supporting reasoning and intra-Hanafi dispute. It begins by stating that a false witness is publicly shamed and not given ta'zir (discretionary lashes) — the punishment is shaming rather than beating. The phrase 'in the market or in his neighborhood with beating and imprisonment' likely refers to the judge's option to physically punish, but the preferred view is shaming. The text then moves to a discussion by Imam al-Hakim Abu Muhammad al-Katib, who classifies the situation of the false witness into three cases: (1) retracting with repentance — no ta'zir by consensus; (2) retracting without repentance — ta'zir by beating by consensus; (3) retraction unknown — disagreement exists, and fatwa is according to Imam Abu Hanifa's view. The passage then addresses acceptance of the false witness's testimony after repentance: if he was a fasiq (sinner), his testimony is accepted after repentance, because his sin was the motive. The duration of repentance is left to the judge. If he was 'adl (just) or mastur (of unknown status), his testimony is never accepted, because the motive for falsehood is unknown. A dissenting view from Abu Yusuf allows acceptance, and this is the preferred position for fatwa. The text concludes with a note that sometimes false testimony is known without confession, as when a person testified to be dead appears alive, showing that ta'zir is not limited to confession. The author then references commentaries (Ayni, Fath, Inaya).

Key Terms
شهود زور (shuhud zoor): False witnesses who deliberately testify to a lie.
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment less than hadd for sins without fixed penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, in which case is a false witness not punished by consensus?
A) When he retracts without repentance.
B) When he retracts with repentance and regret.
C) When his retraction is unknown.
D) When he persists.

Key Takeaway
A false witness's punishment is tailored to his response: shaming is preferred, but beating applies if he persists without repentance.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Acceptance of a False Witness's Testimony After Repentance
Rules for accepting false witness's testimony after repentance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the cases of a fasiq and an 'adl false witness regarding acceptance of their testimony after repentance, and explain why Abu Yusuf's view is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Repentance restores the fasiq's testimony but not the 'adl's — because the motive of the 'adl is unknown.

A false witness who repents may or may not have his testimony accepted. The Hanafi school differentiates based on his prior moral status: if he was a fasiq (sinner), repentance cures the defect; but if he was 'adl (just) or mastur (of unknown status), the motive for falsehood is unknown, so testimony remains rejected. Abu Yusuf held a contrary view that is relied upon in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the starting point: acceptance of a fasiq's testimony
The text says: if the false witness was a fasiq, his testimony is accepted after repentance because his sin was the motive and repentance removes it.
The key term is 'fasiq' – a known sinner.
2
Understand the reasoning for the 'adl/mastur case
If the witness was 'adl or mastur, his testimony is never accepted because the cause for his falsehood is unknown; repentance does not change that.
'Adl means just; mastur means of unknown status.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa held that testimony is never accepted for 'adl/mastur. Abu Yusuf held that it is accepted after repentance. The text states 'wa bihi yufta' (fatwa is given according to Abu Yusuf).
This is a clear tarjih (preference) for the mufti bihi position.
4
Explore the temporal aspect: duration of repentance
Scholars differed on the minimum period of repentance (six months, one year) and imprisonment, but the correct view leaves it to the judge's discretion.
This shows flexibility in ta'zir matters.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a specific background of the false witness (fasiq vs 'adl), determine if his testimony after repentance is accepted and cite the relied-upon view.
Use the distinction and the tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The phrase 'in the market or in his neighborhood with beating and imprisonment' likely refers to the judge's option to physically punish, but the preferred view is shaming. The text then moves to a discussion by Imam al-Hakim Abu Muhammad al-Katib, who classifies the situation of the false witness into three cases: (1) retracting with repentance — no ta'zir by consensus; (2) retracting without repentance — ta'zir by beating by consensus; (3) retraction unknown — disagreement exists, and fatwa is according to Imam Abu Hanifa's view. The passage then addresses acceptance of the false witness's testimony after repentance: if he was a fasiq (sinner), his testimony is accepted after repentance, because his sin was the motive. The duration of repentance is left to the judge. If he was 'adl (just) or mastur (of unknown status), his testimony is never accepted, because the motive for falsehood is unknown. A dissenting view from Abu Yusuf allows acceptance, and this is the preferred position for fatwa. The text concludes with a note that sometimes false testimony is known without confession, as when a person testified to be dead appears alive, showing that ta'zir is not limited to confession. The author then references commentaries (Ayni, Fath, Inaya).

Key Terms
فاسق (fasiq): A person who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, lacking moral integrity.
عدل ('adl): A just person with moral integrity, whose testimony is normally accepted.
مستور (mastur): A person whose moral status is unknown, neither known as just nor sinful.
توبة (tawbah): Repentance from sin, which can restore legal integrity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position, what is the ruling on the testimony of a false witness who was originally 'adl after he repents?
A) It is never accepted.
B) It is accepted.
C) It is accepted only if he was a fasiq.
D) It is accepted only after six months.

Key Takeaway
For a repentant false witness, the decisive factor is his prior status; fatwa follows Abu Yusuf in accepting testimony for all.

Retraction of Testimony: Conditions, Effects, and Liability
Rules for retracting testimony before and after judgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid retraction of testimony and apply the Hanafi rules for the effect of retraction before and after judgment, including liability and ta'zir.

Core Idea
Retraction after judgment does not overturn it, but witnesses must compensate for loss caused.

This lesson examines the Hanafi rulings on a witness retracting their testimony. The key distinction is whether retraction occurs before or after the judge's verdict. Before judgment, it prevents the verdict; after judgment, the verdict stands but the witnesses become liable. We will unpack the definition, condition, and effect of retraction, and understand why the Hanafi school holds witnesses liable even when a judge issued the decrees.

Guided Path
1
Define retraction and its essential elements
Identify the linguistic and technical definition of ruju', its pillar (the witness's statement of falsehood), condition (before a judge), cause (repentance), and ruling (ta'zir and/or liability).
Note: denial is not retraction; only an explicit admission of falsehood counts.
2
Distinguish before and after judgment
Retraction before judgment: judge does not rule based on that testimony. Retraction after judgment: judgment remains valid, but witnesses must compensate (daman) for what they caused to be lost.
The judgment is not overturned because it was already executed; compensation is for the loss inflicted.
3
Identify the cause of liability and the Hanafi reasoning
Liability arises from causing loss (tasbib) even though the judge's action is the direct cause. Hanafi: the judge is compelled (mulja') and cannot be held liable, so the witnesses bear the loss.
This is the basis of the dispute with al-Shafi'i.
4
Contrast the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on liability
Al-Shafi'i holds that since the judge directly executed the judgment, the witnesses are not liable. Hanafi responds by noting the judge's compulsion and the public interest in not deterring judges.
The practical difference: the defendant can recover from witnesses in Hanafi, not in Shafi'i.
5
Apply the ruling to a procedural scenario
Consider cases where retraction is claimed before a non-judge or before a different judge. The text explains when evidence of such retraction is accepted.
Only retraction before the same judge or another judge with jurisdiction is valid.

باب الرجوع عن الشهادة أي في بيان أحكامه لا يصح الرجوع عنها إلا عند قاض، فإن رجعا قبل حكمه، لم يقض، وبعده لم ينقض، وضمنا ما أتلفاه للمشهود عليه الحكم الأول من المال وهو المدعى عليه الشاهدان عن شهادتهما حكم القاضي بشهادتهما باب الرجوع عن الشهادة: الرجوع في اللغة: نقيض الذهاب، واصطلاحا نفي ما أثبته، ثم له ركن: وهو قول الشاهد: شهدت بزور ومثله رجعت عما شهدت به أو كذبت في شهادتي، وإنكارها لا يكون رجوعا، وله شرط: وهو أن يكون عند القاضي، فلا يصح الرجوع عند غيره، وفائدته عدم رجوع البينة على رجوعه، وعدم استحلافه إذا أنكر، وله سبب وهو إرادة التوبة عن شهادة الزور، وحكم وهو وجوب التعزير في غير شهادة الزنا، أما فيها فيجب الحد؛ للقذف منهم سواء كان قبل القضاء أو بعده، الضمان ووجوب مع التعزير بعد القضاء، وقبله التعزير فقط، وسبب الضمان إتلاف المال أو النفس بها، تنزيلاً للسبب منزلة المباشرة، وهو أمر مشروع مرغوب فيه ديانة؛ لأن فيه خلاصاً عن عقاب الكبيرة، وأخره عن شهادة الزور؛ لأن الرجوع عنها يقتضي سبق وجودها. وفي بعض النسخ: "كتاب الرجوع مكان باب الرجوع". (فتح، عناية) يصح إلخ: أي فإذا كان الرجوع عند غيره لا يصح، فلو أقام المقضي عليه بشهادتهما بينة بأنهما رجعا عند غير القاضي أو طلب يمينهما لا تقبل بينته، ولا يحلفان؛ لأنه ادعى رجوعاً باطلاً، بخلاف ما إذا أقرا أنهما رجعا عند غير القاضي حيث يصح إقرارهما، وإن أقرا برجوع باطل؛ لأن إقرارهما به يجعل رجوعاً منهما في الحال، وبخلاف ما إذا أقام البينة أنهما رجعا عند قاض آخر غير الذي كان قضى بالحق حيث يقبل بينته؛ لأنه ادعى رجوعاً صحيحاً [ رمز الحقائق: ١٦١/٢] ولا بد من التقييد بأن القاضي قضى عليهما بالضمان؛ لأنه لو لم يدع المدعى عليه القضاء بالرجوع والضمان لا تسمع منه البينة. (فتح) قاض لأنه فسخ للشهادة فيختص بمجلس الحاكم أي حاكم كان فإن كان الرجوع عند غيره لم يصح. (عيني) لم يقض: أي القاضي بشهادتهما؛ لأن كلامهما متناقض، ولا ضمان عليهما لأحد الخصمين؛ لأنهما لم يتلفا شيئاً على أحد رمز الحقائق: ١٦١/٢] لم ينقض : بالبناء للمجهول أو المعلوم، أي لو رجع الشاهدان بعد حكم القاضي، لم ينقض حكم الحاكم أو لم ينقض القاضي حكمه الأول؛ لترجحه بالقضاء، بخلاف ظهور الشاهد عبداً أو محدوداً في قذف فإن القضاء يبطل، ويرد ما أخذ وتلزم الدية لو قصاصاً ولا يضمن الشهود؛ لما مر أن الحاكم إذا أخطأ فالغرم على المقضي له. (فتح) وضمنا إلخ: وهذا بالإجماع إلا في قول للشافعي لبه : لا ضمان على الشهود؛ لأنه لا عبرة للتسبيب مع وجود المباشرة، قلنا: المباشر هو القاضي ولا يمكن إيجابه عليه؛ لأنه ملجأ إلى القضاء، وفي إيجابه صرف الناس عن وضرر على كافة الناس، فلا يجب الضمان عليه دفعا للضرر عنهم ولا على المدعي؛ لأن الحكم قد مضى، تقليده،
Chapter on Retraction of Testimony, i.e., explaining its rulings. Retraction is not valid except before a judge. If they retract before his judgment, he does not pass judgment; after it, the judgment is not overturned, and they are liable for what they caused to be lost to the party against whom they testified. The first ruling concerning property — and that is the defendant — the two witnesses retract their testimony after the judge's judgment based on their testimony. Chapter on Retraction of Testimony: Linguistically, retraction is the opposite of going; technically, it is negating what one has established. Then it has a pillar: the witness's statement, 'I testified falsely,' and similar statements like 'I retract what I testified' or 'I lied in my testimony.' Denial is not retraction. It has a condition: that it be before a judge; retraction before someone else is not valid. Its benefit: that the witnesses do not retract their retraction and are not required to take an oath if they deny. It has a cause: the desire to repent from false testimony. And a ruling: ta'zir is obligatory except in cases of zina (fornication) testimony, where the hadd (punishment) for qadhf (false accusation) is obligatory, whether before or after judgment. Liability (daman) is obligatory along with ta'zir after judgment; before judgment, only ta'zir. The cause of liability is causing loss of property or life through the testimony, treating the cause like direct action. It is a prescribed and recommended matter from a religious perspective because it delivers from the punishment of major sin. Retraction is placed after false testimony because retraction implies its prior existence. In some versions: 'Kitab al-Ruju'' instead of 'Bab al-Ruju''. (Fath, Inaya). 'Is correct, etc.' means if retraction is made before someone other than the judge, it is not valid. So if the defendant (against whom judgment was passed) produces evidence that they retracted before a non-judge or requests their oath, his evidence is not accepted, and they are not made to swear, because he claims an invalid retraction. But if they admit that they retracted before a non-judge, their admission is valid, even though they admit an invalid retraction, because their admission constitutes a retraction at that moment. And it differs from the case where the defendant produces evidence that they retracted before another judge who did not pass the original judgment: his evidence is accepted, because he claims a valid retraction. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 161/2) It is necessary to restrict that the judge passes judgment of liability on them, because if the defendant does not claim judgment regarding retraction and liability, his evidence is not heard. (Fath). 'Before a judge' because retraction is an annulment of testimony, so it is specific to the court of the judge, any judge. If retraction is before someone other than a judge, it is not valid. (Ayni). 'He does not pass judgment': i.e., the judge does not judge by their testimony because their statements are contradictory, and there is no liability on them towards either litigant because they did not cause loss to anyone. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 161/2) 'It is not overturned' (passive or active): i.e., if the two witnesses retract after the judge's judgment, the judge's judgment is not overturned, or the judge does not overturn his first judgment because it is strengthened by the judgment. Unlike the case where a witness appears to be a slave or one who was punished for qadhf: the judgment is nullified, what was taken is returned, and blood-money becomes due in case of qisas, but the witnesses are not liable, because it has been stated that if the judge errs, the loss is upon the one in whose favor judgment was given. (Fath). 'And they are liable, etc.': This is by consensus except for a statement from al-Shafi'i: there is no liability on the witnesses because causation (tasbib) is irrelevant when there is direct action (mubashira). We say: The direct actor is the judge, and it is impossible to impose liability on him because he is compelled to judge; imposing it would turn people away from judging and harm the entire community. So liability is not obligatory on him to avoid harm to them, nor on the plaintiff because the judgment has passed... his taqlid (appointment).
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on retraction of testimony (bab al-ruju' 'an al-shahada) from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The passage type is a ruling statement with detailed commentary. It begins by defining retraction linguistically and technically, then outlines its pillar (the witness's statement of falsehood), condition (before a judge), benefit (preventing further retraction or oath), cause (repentance from false witness), and ruling (obligation of ta'zir except in zina cases where the hadd of qadhf applies). The key ruling is that retraction before judgment prevents the judge from giving a verdict based on that testimony; retraction after judgment does not overturn the judgment, but the witnesses must compensate for the loss caused to the defendant (e.g., property taken as a result). The commentary then discusses procedural details: if retraction is made before someone other than a judge, it is invalid. If the defendant produces evidence of such retraction, it is not accepted, except in certain cases like if the witnesses admit it or if the retraction was before a different judge. There is also a discussion of liability: after judgment, witnesses must compensate for loss caused, but this is by consensus except for a view of al-Shafi'i who denies liability due to causation not being sufficient when direct action (the judge's decree) exists. The Hanafi response posits that the judge is compelled to judge and cannot be held liable; the witnesses caused the loss indirectly, so they bear it. The passage ends with a note that the ruling is based on taqlid (appointment) of the judge.

Key Terms
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction of testimony, negating what one previously testified.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss caused by false testimony after judgment.
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment applied to false witnesses upon retraction, except in zina cases where hadd applies.
تسبيب (tasbib): Causation; in Hanafi law, causing harm indirectly is treated like direct action in matters of liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, what happens if two witnesses retract their testimony after the judge has already passed judgment based on their testimony?
A) The judgment is overturned and the case is retried.
B) The judgment stands but the witnesses must compensate the defendant for loss caused.
C) The witnesses are given ta'zir but no compensation is required.
D) The judgment is overturned only if the witnesses repent.

Key Takeaway
Retraction after judgment does not overturn it; the witnesses must compensate the loss they caused, based on the Hanafi principle that causation creates liability when the direct actor is compelled.

Retraction of Testimony: Validity and Liability
Ruling on retraction and its consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of retraction of testimony, distinguish between retraction before and after judgment, and explain the liability of witnesses under the principle of tanzil al-sabab manzilat al-mubashirah.

Core Idea
Retraction after judgment does not overturn the ruling, but the witnesses must compensate the defendant.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi doctrine on retraction of testimony. The passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq defines retraction, its conditions, and its legal consequences. A key point is that while the judgment remains binding, the retracting witnesses become liable for any loss caused to the defendant. This ruling is based on istihsan and the principle that causation is given the status of direct action when the direct agent (the judge) is compelled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition and conditions of retraction
Find the pillar (explicit statement) and condition (before the judge) from the passage.
Retraction before anyone else is invalid; denial without explicit retraction is not sufficient.
2
Distinguish effects before and after judgment
Before judgment: the judge does not base his ruling on the retracted testimony; no liability. After judgment: the ruling stands, but witnesses become liable for damages.
The passage emphasizes that the guarantee (damān) is wajib only after the judge's ruling.
3
Understand the basis of liability: tanzil al-sabab manzilat al-mubashirah
The witnesses caused the loss through their testimony; the judge was compelled to rule, so the cause is attributed to them. The analogy of digging a well on a public path illustrates this.
This is a form of qiyās khafī supported by istihsān.
4
Analyze the dispute with Imam al-Shāfi‘ī
Al-Shāfi‘ī holds witnesses not liable because the direct agent is the judge. The Hanafi response: the judge is compelled, and making him liable would harm the judicial system.
The Hanafi position is muftā bihi and supported by consensus except for al-Shāfi‘ī.
5
Apply the ruling to a nuanced scenario
If witnesses retract before another judge, the defendant can bring evidence of that retraction; the second judge's ruling on retraction is valid. However, if the first judge has already ruled, the judgment is not overturned.
The passage includes a specific case: if the defendant claims retraction before another judge, his evidence is accepted because it is a valid retraction.

(فتح) وضمنا إلخ: وهذا بالإجماع إلا في قول للشافعي لبه : لا ضمان على الشهود؛ لأنه لا عبرة للتسبيب مع وجود المباشرة، قلنا: المباشر هو القاضي ولا يمكن إيجابه عليه؛ لأنه ملجأ إلى القضاء، وفي إيجابه صرف الناس عن وضرر على كافة الناس، فلا يجب الضمان عليه دفعا للضرر عنهم ولا على المدعي؛ لأن الحكم قد مضى، تقليده،
Chapter on Retraction of Testimony: Retraction linguistically is the opposite of going; terminologically, it is negating what one has affirmed. It has a pillar: the witness's statement 'I testified falsely' or similar, like 'I retract from my testimony' or 'I lied in my testimony.' Denial of testimony does not constitute retraction. It has a condition: that it be before the judge; retraction before anyone else is invalid. Its benefit is that the testimony does not revert upon his retraction, and he is not sworn if he denies. It has a cause: the desire to repent from false testimony. It has a ruling: the obligation of discretionary punishment (ta'zir) in other than the case of false accusation of zina; as for that case, the fixed punishment (hadd) becomes obligatory for slander, whether before or after the ruling. The guarantee and its obligation accompany the ta'zir after the ruling, while before the ruling only ta'zir applies. The cause of the guarantee is the destruction of property or life through the testimony. This is by giving the cause the status of direct action. It is a legitimate matter, desirable religiously because it contains deliverance from the punishment of a major sin. And it is delayed after false testimony because retraction from it requires its prior existence. In some copies: 'Book of Retraction' in place of 'Chapter of Retraction'. (Fath, 'Inayah) 'Is valid etc.': i.e., if the retraction is before someone else, it is not valid. So if the defendant against whom judgment was passed brings evidence that they retracted before another judge or demands their oath, his evidence is not accepted and they are not sworn, because he claims an invalid retraction. Unlike if they confess that they retracted before another judge, in which case their confession is valid, even if they confess an invalid retraction, because their confession makes it a retraction presently. And unlike if he brings evidence that they retracted before another judge other than the one who passed judgment, in which case his evidence is accepted, because he claims a valid retraction. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 161/2] And it is necessary to restrict that the judge passed judgment on them regarding the guarantee, because if the defendant does not claim the ruling of retraction and guarantee, his evidence is not heard. (Fath) 'Judge' because retraction is an annulment of testimony, so it is specific to the court of the ruler, any ruler. (Ayni) 'did not rule' i.e., the judge does not decide based on their testimony because their speech is contradictory, and there is no guarantee upon them for either litigant because they did not destroy anything. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 161/2] 'is not overturned' in the passive or active voice, i.e., if the two witnesses retract after the judge's ruling, the ruling of the judge is not overturned or the judge does not overturn his initial ruling, because it is strengthened by the ruling. Unlike the appearance that the witness is a slave or had been punished for slander, for then the ruling is nullified, what was taken is returned, and the blood money is necessary if it was retaliation, but the witnesses are not liable because the judge is the one who erred and the liability is on the beneficiary. (Fath) 'And they guarantee etc.': This is by consensus except for a statement of al-Shafi'i: there is no guarantee on the witnesses because causation is not considered when there is direct agency. We respond: The direct agent is the judge, and it is not possible to impose it upon him because he is compelled to judge, and imposing it would turn people away from undertaking the office and cause harm to all people. So the guarantee is not obligatory on him to avoid harm to them, nor on the plaintiff because the ruling has passed, and his reliance on it.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter on retraction of testimony from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It defines the legal term 'ruju'', its pillar (the witness's explicit statement of retraction), condition (being before a judge), cause (repentance), and rulings (ta'zir or hadd for false accusation, and guarantee of damages). The key rulings: retraction is valid only before the judge; if the witnesses retract before the judge's ruling, the judge does not decide based on that testimony; if they retract after the ruling, the ruling is not overturned, but the witnesses must compensate the defendant for any loss incurred. The commentary addresses a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i: al-Shafi'i holds that the witnesses are not liable because the direct cause of the loss is the judge's ruling, but the Hanafi position is that the witnesses are liable because the judge was compelled to rule, and making the judge liable would harm the institution of judging. This is based on the principle of 'giving the cause the status of direct action' (tanzil al-sabab manzilat al-mubashirah), analogous to digging a well on a public path: the digger is liable even though someone else caused the fall. The passage also clarifies that if the witnesses retract but the judge has not yet passed judgment, they are not liable because no loss has occurred. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah as the matn is from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, which is based on authentic Hanafi texts.

Key Terms
الرجوع عن الشهادة (al-ruju' an al-shahada): Legally, it is the witness's negation of his previously given testimony before the judge.
التسبيب (al-tasbīb): Causation (indirect action) that is given the legal status of direct action to establish liability.
الضمان (al-damān): Financial liability or compensation for loss caused by the witness's testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for retraction of testimony to be valid in Hanafi fiqh?
A) It must be made publicly.
B) It must be made before the judge who heard the case.
C) It must be made with the consent of the plaintiff.
D) It must be made within three days of the testimony.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that retraction of testimony after judgment does not invalidate the judgment but makes the witnesses liable for compensation, based on the principle of causation (tanzīl al-sabab manzilat al-mubāshirah).

Shahadat — Testimony
